O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	You, three sons, I have fulfilled this book that is behind the science of medicine the fulfillment of it, and have ended it through its exposures and by its declarations.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And I saw that I have fulfilled this with the surgery, which is from the hands of women, it is to say "surgery".
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And because the work of women is disturbed in our region and is disfigured as a whole, if it is perceived by science and practice, and there is nothing more to do than the small descriptions in books written by the hands of the ancients that have moved.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And it has come to this error and vanity, and the intentions are closed and science is alienated.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation; et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	I seem to think that I will revive this by assembling the order of this cauterization according to the way of exposition and declaration and abbreviation; and I will assemble the forms of the burners of the cautery and other instruments of the work with the adjustment of the declaration and preparation of it, as it is his craft.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And because no skilled hands masters are found in our ten, the art of medicine is extended.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And it is necessary for him who enters the science of anatomy, as Galen says, to know the judgment of the bones, and their forms and conjunctions and separations of us, and to have knowledge of the bones, nerves, and limbs, and the number of our joints, and the movement and rest of the limbs, and the issue of the same.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc; et meismement en l’art de main.	And for this reason, Iocras says that the non with the non is not together, and with the hand it is few; and at the same time in the art of the hand.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes; ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	In the introduction of this book, we say that who are not acquainted with these things, if they do not err and do not harm men; for I have many times seen these who enter into this science and abandon it and its sense and experience.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa I apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col; por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	For I see a man who cuts off the penis of a woman or from the neck of a woman, and cuts the arteries of the neck; because so much blood issues out that the woman dies in her own hands.
Et vis I autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans; si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens III jors.	And see if another man who treads on a wound of an old man, and the wound was big; if it is carried with him a piece of the bladder, and he died in three hours.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	I have already been accused of the cautery, and see the position of the patient and the size of the wound, and if it was cut well, he died.
Et vis I autre mire qui prist en cure I duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie; et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi I termine; et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie; et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	And see if another man who was in the care of our king, who had a broken leg, and with the splint he had a wound; and the ignorant ones tightened the break on the wound as soon as possible, and did not leave the wound any slack, and they left it to heal; and he commanded that he not loosen it; and afterwards it was all swollen and the bone and came to ruin.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe; et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	I am called to come to him, and I hurried to come remove the leg; and when I free it if it was not in pain and did not feel any pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner; et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	But all the way the corruption was confirmed or member, and could not be healed; and the corruption did not stop until the member was completely lost.
Et vis I autre mire qui effondra I apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And see another mirror that will crumble and fall in amazement, and then burns because of the malice of his lordship.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	For chancre, when he is free of melancholic humor, only then does one dare to touch it with iron if it is not in its entirety that can heal what is corrupted.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en II divisions: c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions; et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	For this reason, careful women, you should know that the work of hands is divided into two divisions: it is knowledge, either to have or to have danger in other dispositions; and I will show each of you in this book where there is fear and danger.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez; et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit; et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	For this reason, you should be careful that you keep yourself in good order, so that the enemy may not speak ill of you. Take your weapons and armor, and put on your armor lightly but firmly, and use the best way possible for the grace of God to save you and make you strong; and let the unwholesome diseases of grief be cured; and keep your weapons in order so that you may come out of this world with glory.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens: «Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.	The first sentence translates to: "Galen says in his admonitions: 'Do not take medicine for serious illness, lest you become the laughingstock of the ignorant.'
» J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc III chapitres.	This translates to: "I have read this treatise according to three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez; et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	The first chapter is about fire cauteries and hot medicine cauteries, and it is ordered from the head down to the feet; and forms of stings, and burns with cauteries, and all that is necessary in the work.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses; et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	The second chapter is about cutting and piercing, and ventouses and wounds, and extraction of arrows, and similar things; and it is ordered and the forms of stings.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses; et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	The third chapter is about restoring dislocations and twists, and similar things; and it is ordered by the main doctor's hands, and the forms of the sprains.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	However, it is necessary that we remember the work, I will give the quality of the help and the benefit for each complexity.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus; et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu; et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	I say that the quality of the help and benefit is the longest word and subtle science and the secret remedy; and because of this, more people speak of their wounds and agree with them; and they say less words because I do not want to repeat myself.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que II complexions: c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	I say that cauterization helps universally with all complexions or matters, for whatever the complexion: it is to know hot complexions with matter, and dry complexions with matter.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide; et li autre dirent le contraire: que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	In hot and dry complexions, no one and everyone says that cauterization is of great help; and the other says the opposite: that cauterization is only good for diseases that come from chlorine and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour; et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	For the nature of fire is hot, and should not be treated for hot diseases with chlorine, nor with dryness; and that is what the one who says the opposite says, that cauterization helps greatly with hot diseases that come from the courage of men.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	For when you perceive the heart of the man and his moisture at the complexion of fire, you truely see the heart's color.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree with this word.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	For I have never found it at any time by experience.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens; des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	And every way, it does not interfere with anything more than he who has experienced it and knows by long practice the chapter of cauteries, and the diversity of complexions of men, and their dispositions and causes of their diseases, and their symptoms and their spaciousness; for other complexions we have no power, just as in cold and moist diseases.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And they were able to resemble and align with the cauterization.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	Understand, children, that cauterization is possible with fire if it is a secret of the healing arts, and even more beneficial than the ardent medicine of cauterization.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For the fire is simple, and only comes as harm to the member that is cooked, and does not harm any other member.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation; et par aventure ocit lou malaide Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	The ardent medicines come from one member to another by allaying, and bring the miseries of the malady to health; and by chance often the patient has too much fire in his substance, but it does not harm if there is no excess.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses; et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant; or le recevez en vos pensees.	1. And I found this in my research through experimentation and the length of service and study I have dedicated to this art, and it is true; and for this I apologize for the length of the word, as I only want to share with you the secret that is hidden or fire, and the quality of the work, as it treats the diseases of the body, just as the philosopher says by demonstrating; and receive it in your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	1. Know, son, that the cauteries should be made in the right manner and with proper tools.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere; et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	1. I say that cauterization is useful in all cases because the wounds are not properly healed by the aid of cauterization; and moreover, if the cauterization is done for necessary pains and hurts that cannot wait for the time that greatest malice does not come to the member.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire; car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue; et il le dient ensi; mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	1. And do not think otherwise, it is the same as the folk say; for the disease that is cured by cauterization has no return; and he says thus, but it is not so if one cares, because cauterization is only a medicine that dries the complexion, and drys the humors that cause the pain, and is worthy of medicine for the hasty death of one's valor, and for the virtue of one's work and ladyship.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut; et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie; mais ce avient poc.	1. However, it is certain that the disease does not return once the complexion of the sick person and the lesion of the disease are dried by cauterization; and they are assembled in him, the superfluities being acquired through the acquisition of meat and such things, unless cauterization is administered to him or he has little superfluity and moisture, as with cauterization for pain, and the wounds, and only some pain does not return; but this is rare.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir; mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	1. And many people do not understand that cauterization is a part of medicine, and this is seen; but they only believe that cauterization is after medicine, but we understand it is false, and cauterization is a part of medicine because when we administer remedies for any disease and they do not work, we then use cauterization, and it works.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	2. Therefore, it is well that cauterization is part of medicine, even if some people do not understand it.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance; et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes; et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	3. The ancients said that cauterization made of gold was as bad as iron, and they said this was due to the quality of the gold and the high content of its substance; and they said that the use of gold cautery did not cause any harm, but it is true because I have experienced it and found that it is true in some people; and gold cautery is as good as iron, as they say.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez; et s’on le chaufe trop; si font au feu; et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	And when you hold the instrument of gold, you do not know if it is heated by the color of the gold, and when it has cooled down; and if it is too hot, then it burns in the fire; and then it has enough resistance.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And that's why we use our fire cauterization that we have made in our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	Or if you have ordered this chapter of the loose joints, because it is easier to find.
dou cautere olivaire	Olive cauterization.
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	Olive cauterization is used for moisture and coldness in the head, and when it is caused by a disease called "soda", and by many humors that descend to the joints of the head, ears, and eyes, and numerous dreams and pain in the throat and jaw, and also for all diseases that come from coldness, such as paralysis, stroke, and apoplexy, and similar diseases.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief III nuis ou IIII, selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir; et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	The form of this cauterization is as follows: if the patient is purged by solvent medicine modifying the third or fourth degree of the wood, according to which the virtue and the ease and accustoming of the patient can bear; then I repeat the dose of the medicine.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis; aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses II eulz; et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	Then place the root of your palm between the root of his nail and its two fingers; and if you see your two means, if it bleeds, then wash the cauterization called "olive," which is of the form:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant; puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os I sol petit; et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit; aprés pren I poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse III jors; aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre; et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then place the ink of the pen between the nail and its two fingers; and if you see your two means, if it bleeds, then wash the cauterization called "olive," which is of the form: Then apply ink to the hand, and gently press on the hand with the other hand, and if you see the bone, then continue the cauterization as long as you see the bone as I told you; then take a piece of cloth, and soft cotton, and put it on the nail, and leave it for three days; then apply a poultice of the ointment called "tetrafarmacon," as long as it is healthy.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge; et por ce si aide mues.	And they say to the ancient one, that the more tense the wound is, the more it bleeds; and therefore it helps to aid it.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And no one of these says that the fire cautery should be so tight that part of the bone is broken off, and then remove what is broken off from the bone, and treat it.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme I vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors; et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte; aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	And they say that the fire cautery should be so tight that it breaks the bone, and then bind it strongly to the bone, and treat it. Afterward, it must be treated for a long time overstretched; then it must be cured and dressed.
Et ces II manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor; et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier; car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres; et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	1. These two methods of cauterization do not seem to be the best in general, despite their effectiveness in certain cases; and I feel that I should leave them alone, as the head of the shoulder is often affected by continuous natural solutions, as we have experienced in other parts of the body; and even when the patient's strength is weak by nature, the first appearance of cauterization seems to be more salve and less painful to me, and for that reason I use it in this way.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	2. of the ancient pain of the head
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres; et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	3. When the whole head is afflicted with chronic pain that lasts for a long time, and it must be used with the patient's consent and the pills called "cochie," and purging of the head and oils and plasters; and if the cauterization is done as we have said before, and it does not work, then it is not worth it.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit; adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	When the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai I cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»; et est I leus en coi on met ventouses; et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os: li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors; et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	After making the cauterization on each eye of the shoulder bone as we have described, and then making the cauterization on the eye that is called "vassels"; and these are those that are put in a vacuum; and hold your hand so that you do not see the bone: the patient feels too much pain in this cauterization than in others, and I will explain later; and it is necessary that the cauterizations of the eyes be more subtle than those made on the shoulder joint, and this is the form:
dou cautere dou chief	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie: adonques li fai cauteres selonc II manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	When sudden pain comes from the cautery, and the disease spreads to the oil, and the head is purged with medicines modified, and the other cures I have mentioned in the division of diseases are made, but none of them benefit: therefore, I did cauterizations in two ways, that is, with hot and dry medicine.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope I poc as II chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir; et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi XII houres; et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi II jors ou III; puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	If you apply a poultice of alum with medicine that is hot and dry, and it draws out the pus and the wound, then open the temple and place the poultice on the painful part in such a way that you can replace the alum poultice later; when it is replaced, if the patient holds it well and leaves it for 12 hours, then remove it and apply a poultice of comfrey, leaving the wound open for 2 or 3 days; then cover the wound with a moist cloth until it is healed.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	After the treatment of wounds as soon as it is healthy; and if you see that I write any other remedies that I have written or treat some remedies that are harmful.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere.	The fire cautery is used according to this method.
Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	Heat the cautery and its form is:
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait I poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance; et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse; et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	And it is called "closed" because the head is made in the shape of a clout or has a hole like a raven's beak, and appears small; and it is placed on the painful part, and hold the patient's hand and lightly press the iron with one hand while the other half of the edge is raised as high as possible; and gently lift your hand when the artery is no longer red, that is cooled, and there is an abundance of blood.
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par III jors; puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	After putting cotton on the needle, and then insert the limb three times; then put fine cotton in the burrow, and then treat the limb with ointment as it becomes healthy; and if you return to cauterize this wound with the cauterization tool called "cultellare" at all points, and keep away from the artery in this wound that is not yet angry.
de emigraine	of the wound
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans; et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez; et laisse l’uevre em mi voie; mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre. de la torture de la bouche	of the torture of the mouth
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie; et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	Torture that must be treated with fire cautery is only those that move due to fleas, as we have mentioned in divisions of the disease; and do not make cautery like those that come from scratching and spasm of nerves.
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de III cauteres: l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des II levres; et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce; et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	When you treat this appearance of torture that is silent of fleams from wounds and exudations of the cheek and gargle, and it is not worth, then it comes to your attention that you must cauterize the patient with three burns: one at the root of the ear, another on the temple, and the third in the jaw; and place the cauterization in the part that opens naturally, and make the cauterization so that the tip of the ear is in a hole made by the corner of the cheek, and another in the temple as long as possible; and leave the cauterization as much as half of it is burned; and this is the form of the cauterization.
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros; aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the resemblance of the cuttlefish we have placed before you is, but it is a more subtle one and it should be that the cuttlefish is a bit larger; after treating the limb as I have said, as soon as it is healthy.
Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai IIII cauteres: II sus les II cornes dou chief, et I emmi le chief, et I ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac; et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant. de la froidor dou chief	Of the cold head

de l’epilempsie	Of the epilepsy

de la cure de fistule par cautere	Of the cure of fistula by cauterization
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When you treat fistula as we have said in the division of diseases, and your treatments do not benefit, therefore it comes that you must cauterize it according to this method.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain; et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief; aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil; aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz: et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere; se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente; mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	Instruct the patient to cut his hair close to his head; and trim the beard around your hands in such a way that it does not move or fall out; then apply cotton wool soaked in olive oil or persillon juice to the wound; then heat the cauterization instrument that has been divided: and cauterize the hair if it forms like a penpoint of voutoul, assemble the cauterization as the hair; if you see, if one end is cut off from the other, and if you see, if it is like a tent; but always, this that is cauterized is enough for your cure.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche; et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe; aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie; et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	After pressing the fistula, it swells and the exudate dries out, and if it closes, it causes the belly to ache; then form the fire cautery, and place your hand on the cautery at the part where the oil is suspended from the belly, so that your hands do not get greasy; then put the cautery in the oil grease, and it corrupts.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien.	If you come to the beginning of the fire cautery against the bone, it would be good.
Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse III jors; aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se XL jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers; et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	If not, then repeat the fire cautery once more, and if you must, and leave it for three days; then put on cotton wool in the bure, and apply the desiccating ointment as soon as it is dry, and when 40 days have passed and it is dry, if the bone is exposed, then apply an acrid medicine until the bone is covered; and follow according to what comes in your chapter.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent.	And there is a way of cauterizing fistulas that no ancient one said.
Entens a fistule, et fens le leu; aprés met en la fendure I camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	Under the fistula, and put in the forceps; then insert the subtle cautery of this form:
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc; et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil; et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe: li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	And they make it to the quantity of an 'Z' of plonc; and hold your hand firmly on the cautery, and do not move the patient at all, only when the ploncs are melted, and do not touch the oil with your fingers; and it is necessary to put the oil on clean linen or cotton in the abscess or wound of the fistula, and the patient will be healthy for mervillouse health.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin.	If the fistula is healed by the cauterization we have described, that is good.
Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	If not, then it is necessary to administer tetanus to the newborn, and bring the fistula back to the corium of the newborn according to what is appropriate for the own lear.
des crevaices en levres	cracks in the lips
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	Many times cracks in the lips are called "scalds", and at the same time in the lips of children.
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe I petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	When you treat these cracks according to what we have described in divisions, and the patient does not improve, then use a small fire cauterization according to this form:
Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu’il viegne jusc’a font; aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And he puts them in those cracks as soon as they arrive; after treating the wound with salve until it is healthy.
de l’aposteme de la goule	of the abscess of the gall
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule; et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie: adonques covient il que tu aies I cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule; aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu; et fai ensi une fois ou II, aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	When an abscess comes in the root of the gallbladder or uterus, or testicle, or roots of teeth, and it becomes inflamed and forms a fistule; and you treat it as we have said in divisions, and it does not profit: therefore, it is necessary that you cauterize according to the size of the fistule; after the bog or abscess is drained, and hold your hand until the fire cautery reaches the font of the fire, and when it is done; and once or twice, after treating as we have said in treatments, until it is healthy; and if it is cured once or twice, it is good; and if not, it is necessary to expose the wound and open the corrupted bone, according to what you will find in his chapter.
dou movement des dens	The first sentence to translate is: "Ou cautere
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain; aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent; et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent; aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit; aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and you cure them with medicines and it does not work, then place the dislocated tooth in your mouth; afterwards wash the cauterization that formed on it, in such a way that you put a thread around the tooth; and pull out the dislocated teeth gently, and hold your hand tightly so that the patient feels the pain coming from the root of the tooth; afterwards gently release your hand and continue the cauterization according to your will; afterwards fill the patient's mouth with salty water, and paint it once an hour and rinse thoroughly.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	And in part, the teeth that were moving are confirmed, and the gum becomes softened restricted, and the moisture is corroded dried up.
de la dolor des dens	of the pain of the teeth
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc II manieres: et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	When pain in the teeth comes from cold, or if it is cold or visible, and the care of medicine does not help, then it has a duty to cauterize according to two ways: and cauterization by fire and cauterization by brimstone.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain; aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez; et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus I fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	Cauterization by brimstone if it is such that you prefer brimstone over wool, and the end in a iron or steel cup; then take cotton and envelope around the point of a needle, and make the wool burn, and place it on the painful tooth firmly and hold until it is cooled; and often I do this as long as the virtue lives at the root of the tooth, and if you see that the wool and cotton in brimstone are burning, and place it on the tooth, and place iron charged as much as the flesh lives in the chew of the tooth.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide; aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez; fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain.	1. The fire cautery is applied if it is such that you preheat a piece of iron or copper, and it is large so that the fire does not reach the patient's mouth; afterwards, hold the cautery, and then place it on the tooth and keep your hand there until the cautery is cooled down; do this often because the pain will be eased for you or the next day.
Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And it is necessary that the patient fills their mouth with hot brimstone in the pressure of this cautery, and then it becomes red; and this is the form of the cautery.
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir; et c’est li forme de la caine:	And make the cut of the kind you want, and according to what you have to do; and this is the form of the knife:
des scrophules	of scrophules
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait II aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie; et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou II se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume; et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi III jors; et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee; aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the scrophules are soft and cold, and do not respond to digestion by medicines, then sharpen the knife's edge after it comes into form, and make two openings for the fumes to escape from the other side; and place the knife's edge on the abscess once, or as it may be, until it reaches the point of the abscess; and if the abscess is small, then put the knife according to the quantity of the abscess, and leave it for three days; and wipe the blade with a soft cloth as often as it is used; after which cure the patient of wounds and infections until he is healthy.
Li forme de la cainne:	The first sentence to translate is: "Ou cautere de feu comande au mala
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives; aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc.	When the moistors win against the hard parts of the joints, and at the same time when it comes from a cold complexion, then the patient must first have the hot cautery removed by soluble medicines; after that, I will do the cauterization at the base of the throat, and make sure you don't come too close to the throat, and only burn a little bit.
Aprés li fai I autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant; et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	After that, I will do another cauterization at the joint of the other end of the spine, and it is called the "clavicle"; and cure the limb as we have said, as long as it is healthy.
de la toust	Of the entire
Quant tous et maladie de pormon sont de moistors froides, et li malaides nen ait fievre ne sechor, et est li maladie anciaine, se li fai ij cauteres sus la forcele en leus vuis; et I autre cautere emmi le pis entre II mameles; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» selonc la forme qui est devant dite.	When all the diseases of the face are caused by cold moisture, and the patient has no fever or sweating, and it is an old disease, then make incisions with the fire cautery on the parts you wish; and the other cautery is called "clavicle" according to the form that is mentioned.
Et se tu vues, fai cautere en poignant a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins» de coi li forme est ci devant en la maladie des oreilles; et soient li poins jusc’a XXX, ou enqui entor.	And if you see, make incisions by pricking at the entire cautery called "points" of the form that is mentioned in the disease of the ears; and let the points be as many as 30, or more.
Aprés cure le leu selonc ceu qui est devant dit, et soit li cauteres a III rains selonc ceste forme:	After treating the limb according to what is mentioned before, and let the cautery be made with three rains according to this form.
Et por ceu sont li cautere plus legier, por ceu que tu en fais III a cop.	And for this reason, the fire cautery is lighter, because you do it three times with a copper needle.
de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement.	When the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation.
Aprés soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos et sus son costeit; aprés lieve le keur qui est dedens le titillite as dois de ta main senestre; et se li jointure est desaluee dedens, si eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners douqueil ci est li forme:	After you have removed the patient's clothing and their coat; after loosening the knot that tightens the titillation, it is your left hand that should now touch; and if the joint is dislocated, this is the form of the cautery:
et cauterize lou keur tant qu’il le perce jusc’a costeit, et venrait li fugure dou cautere ensamble IIII cauteres; et por ceu est faite cautere avec le cautere qui a III ners, por coi li figure de cauterization sunt sis cauteres; et sont li nerf selonc la subtiliteit d’une tente et c’est li forme dou cautere qui a III ners:	When the knee is to be cauterized, until it pierces the costal cartilage, and then the force of the cauterization comes together in four points; and this is done with a cauterizing iron that has three nails, because the appearance of cauterization is six points; and these nails are according to the fineness of a tent stake and this is the form of the cauterizing iron that has three nails:
Et aucune fois est ajostez sus ce I nerf por coi il i a VIII cauteres.	And no time has it been adjusted to this nerve because it has eight cauterizations.
Aprés met sus le cautere porrelz broiez avec seil; aprés fai reposer le malaide, et ne soit meus li membres par lonc tens tant qu’il soit bien confortez.	After putting the cauterizing iron on the nerve with silk, and then letting the patient rest, and do not force the limbs as long as they are well comforted.
Et s’il est desaloiez desus, liquelz chose avient poc, adonques fait cautere sus l’epaisse dou cautere clavile, ou mout de cauteres en poignant.	If it is dislocated, something comes out quickly, so it is done on the large fire cautery clamp or by touching the cauterizing point.
Car li jointure est refermee, et est ostee li moistor et est sanez li malaides.	For the joint is closed, and is affected by moisture and is not hurt by the patient.
Quant en l’estomac vienent froidures et mout de moistors tant qu’il l’estraient a sa complexion, et sont multipliet li catharre a lui, et es manieres de cures acostumees et il ne profite mie, adonc covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son dos, et estende ses jambes et ses mains.	When coldness and moisture come to the stomach, as it is drawn towards its complexion, and are multiplied in the catharsis to it, and according to customary cures, and it does not benefit, then it is necessary that the patient be seated on his back, extended his legs and arms.
De ceu en aprés li fai III cauteres I desoz la cuillier dou pis per la quantiteit d’un doi, a tout le cautere clavile, et II cauteres defuers les II costez tant que li figure des cauteres soit a III angles, et ait teil espaice entre l’une et l’autre qu’elles ne soient jointes ensamble quant elles giteront porriture; et soient li cautere si parfont qu’il porpreignent les II pars dou keur, et soit li figure des cauteres selonc ceste forme sens ajostement:	1. For this reason, I made three burns on the heel of the foot due to its quantity, at all the cauterization points, and two cauterizations on the knees so that the cauterizations are at least three angles apart and have some space between them so they do not stick together as they sweat; and these cauterizations should be made so that they touch the two parts of the heel, and the figure of the cauterizations should be like this:
Et se tu vues cauterize d’un grant cautere enmi l’estomac selonc ceste forme; et celui qui avra paour de cest cautere, cauterize en poignant et seigne sus l’estomac i. point selonc la quantiteit que tu vues d’enche; puis le cauterize a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins».	2. And if you see to cauterize the stomach with a large burn according to this form; and the one who suffers from this cauterization, cauterize by touching and seizing on the stomach at the point where you see the quantity that you see; then cauterize all the points that are called "points".
Aprés le cure de la cure que nos avons eut devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the cure we had before, as long as it is healthy.
Quant au foie vient dolor de froit et de moistor et de grosse ventositeit, tant qu’il est fuer mis de sa complexion natureil per les superfluitez; et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne li profite mie, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son haitereil; et signe d’enche III cauteres selonc ceste forme et ceste figure et ceste quantiteit sus lou foie, defuer les ypocondres, lai ou li coutes de l’ome vient; et ait d’espaice entre chaicun cautere la groissece d’un doi; et soient li cautere dou lonc dou cors, et ne presser mie mout ta main a tot le cautere; et soit arse tant soulement li moitiez dou keur, et soit li malaides drois sus ses piez; et s’il ne peut, si soit gisans, et estende ses jambes, et lieve ses brais; et c’est li forme:	After the liver comes pain in the head and moisture and large ventosity, as long as it is properly placed according to its natural complexion due to superfluities; and the patient is treated as we have said in divisions, and if he does not profit from it, then the patient should be cured with cauteries according to this form and this figure and this quantity on the liver, deferring the gout of the spleen, whether the blood comes from the stomach or the head; and there should be space between each cauterization of a certain growth of a doe; and they should be long enough in the belly, and not press too hard with your hand on the cauterization; and it should only be half of the liver, and it should be on its own feet; and if it cannot, then it is best if it is extended, and spreads its legs, and lowers its breasts; and this is the form:
Et se ta volentez est, si cauterize ces cauteres dou cutellaire, se tu es subtilz et saiges en l’art, et te warde que tu n’ardes mie tout le keur, car tu feroies sechier tout le cors; et qu’il ne viegne jusc’a boueil, car li keurs est mout subtilz lai endroit, et lou saiches por voir.	If your desire is to burn these cauteries of the dull type, if you are subtle and gentle in the art, and you want to spare all the skin, because you will dry out the entire body; and that it does not become dusty, because the hair is very delicate everywhere, and you want to see.
Quant il a apostume au foie, et tu vues savoir s’il est en la char dou foie ou en la toile: s’il est en la char, se sent li malaides dolor ne mie trop fort; et s’il est en la toile, si sent dolor forsenee.	When it has ascended to the liver, and you see if it is in the liver or on the cloth: if it is in the liver, it feels the pain of the great pain but not too much; and if it is on the cloth, it feels sudden pain.
Et lors quant ceste cure desoit les mires, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus sa teste; et puis seigne d’enche le leu ou li apostumes est, et puis chaufe le cautere qui est semblans au rais, de coi ci est li forme:	When this treatment is complete and the patient has regained consciousness, if the shoulder is swollen; then raise the arm or the affected part, and then heat the cautery which resembles a raisin, according to what is appropriate.
Et cauterize I cautere tant que li keurs soit ars, et viegne jusc’a syphac, tant que li porreture soit toute fuers; aprés la cure selonc la cure des essues tant qu’il soit sanez; et ne covient mie que de cest cautere use nuls fuers que cil qui ait estudieit longement en l’art de medicine, et par cui mains cestes maladies ont corrut aucune fois.	And cauterize the cauterization until the skin is burned, and it comes off easily, as long as the wound is clean; after the treatment according to the treatment of fluids as long as it is healthy; and only this cautery should be used without any other means than those who have studied for a long time in the art of medicine, and by these hands these diseases have never been corrupted once.
Adonques puet il hardiement ovrer, et toutevoies il me semble que mues vaut li laissier.	Indeed, it is not easily overcome, and it seems that it is better to leave it.
dou cautere de pleuresin	For the cure of wounds caused by thorns
Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d’aristologe, et en teil maniere: pren une racine d’aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois; et la moille en oile, et l’emprens au feu, et cauterize I cautere entre la forcele et lou col, et II petis cauteres un poc en dessendant en la partie qui est desoz la barbe; et II cauteres entre la quinte coste et la sisime, en declinant derrier un poc; et I cautere emmi le pis, et I autre sus l’estomac, et I entre II espaules, et II as II costez dou pis defuers le cautere qui est entre II espaules; et ne presser mie ta main, ains fai apertement ausi com en odorant.	It was said that one should use aristolochia roots for the cure of wounds caused by thorns: first, find a long, dry, and very large root of aristolochia, and cut it into small pieces; then heat it in oil, and apply it to the wound between the forceps and the collar, and make two or three cauterizations as you descend in the area that is raw around the beard; make a cauterization between the fifth ribs and the seventh, descending on the back of the pouch; cauterize the pis, and the other in the stomach, and between the shoulders, and the costal pits that the cautery is in between the shoulders; do not press too hard with your hand, as you would with a smell.
Et dirent aucun ancien que aucun home usent de cautere de feir semblant a I raseur, et l’eschaufent et le mettent entre les costes, tant qu’il vient a cel aposteme; et saut fuers li dolor, si com nos avons dit en l’aposteme dou foie.	And no ancient one said that no man used a fire cautery like the rasping, and they thrust it and place it between the ribs, as soon as it comes to the abscess; and the pain is felt, as we have said in the abscess of the liver.
Mais en cestui ovraige est paour ou li malaides muert maintenant, ou fistule i vient qui ne puet estre sanee.	However, in this case, there is pain or the patient has died now, or a fistula comes that cannot be saved.
de la mice	of the mouse.
Quant tu cures la maladie de la mice de ceu que nos avons dit as divisions des cures, et il ne profite mie, adonques i afierent III manieres de cautere que tuit sont boin.	When you treat the disease of the mouse as we have described, and it does not profit much, therefore there are three ways of cauterization that you have mentioned.

After burning the two nerves until they are perceived from the other side, and then use the cautery, and afterwards insert it at four places. Aprés le cure quant il a geteit porriture par lonc tens, et ce vaut mues que li autre des cures devant dites.	After the cure when it has gotten rid of the grease by long tense, and this is enough that the other cures are said to be done.
de ydropisie	of dropsy.
Cautere ne vaut a ydropique, fors c’a la maniere qui est apelee «asclytes».	Cauterization is not good for dropsy, for it is called "ascites.
Quant tu la cures selonc les manieres que nos avons dit en divisions, et ta cure ne profite mie, adonques covient il que tu li faices IIII cauteres entor la boude, et I sus l’estomac, et un sus le foie, et I sus la mice, et II derrier le dos sus l’espinee, et I endroit le pis; et soit li cauteres bien pres de l’espés dou keur.	When you cure according to the methods we have said in divisions, and your cure does not benefit, then it is necessary that you make four caustics at the bowels, and one at the stomach, and one at the liver, and one at the gallbladder, and one at the back of the spine, and one at the hip joint; and make sure the cauterization is close to the end of the curve.
Aprés laisse le cautere aovert por giter porriture lonc tens, et ne lassier mie la cure dou malaide aprés le cautere; et sanation se hasterait, et seront ensamble les II ententions avec l’aide de Deu.	After the cauterization, let the patient drink long and thin broth, and do not delay the treatment of the wounded after the cauterization; and healing will speed up, and the two understandings will be gathered together with the help of God.
Li forme dou cautere por le ventre soit li clavile que nos avons devant mostreit; et cil por le dos soit olivaire, selonc ceu qu’il est ci devant mis.	The form of the cauterization is made on the abdomen, either by the rib that we show before; and on the back, it is olive-shaped, according to what is in front of it.
de l’enfleure des piez	of the enflaming of the wounds
Quant li piez sont enflez a celui qui est ydropique, et sont plain d’awe citrine, il covient que tu cauterizes sus le dos dou piet entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire; et lieve ta main avec le cautere sens torner.	When the wounds are inflamed by water, and they are full of greenish pus, it is necessary to cauterize on the back of the wound between the auricle and the anus; and gently hold the cauterization tool with the cautery so as not to turn.
Et n’entrer mie trop em parfont, ensi sarrait fuers li awe citrine, et soit li cauteres selonc cest forme:	And do not enter too much, otherwise it will be too rough for the awl, and the fire cautery should be made according to this form:

de la menoison	of the mustard

de la dolor dou dos	Of the pain of the back
