After curing the wound as much as it is healthy according to what we have said, and after you are instructed not to use fire cauterization that is in the form of spame of nerf.
de la dolor des jointes	of the pain of joints
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When the pain of joints comes from moisture that is spread to each part of the body, and when the pain comes with cold cause and medicines do not cure it, then it is cured by cauterization in this way: make a cut around the joint of the pain, and if it is olive oil according to this form:
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point».	And if you see that you prick at the face of the child, then perform the burn with the entire burn as claimed "point".
Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil III cauteres ou IIII de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if the pain comes to the groin and other joints, and this happens many times, then perform the burn on each groin III cauteres or IV of each part, on all the olive cauterization; and if you have skill for more, but do not hold your hand until it is as much as it hurts.
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre.	And if the pain descends to the groin and the back, apply the burn we have described in this chapter.
Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile II lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines.	And if the pain remains in the hands, I make points every second line; and if there is no more pain, I make points on each joint and on the hair of the hand; and if the pain comes as fleets or as shoulder pains, cauterize each part, and govern the patient's behavior with medicine.
Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	For if you govern the patient's behavior with medicine and purge the fumes, they will be cured by God's grace.
de la routure dou syfac	of the rupture of the face.
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When the rupture comes in waves, and the blisters descend as clouds and it is new, then if you think that when you see him cured, he will not return to his place; and that he uses things that relieve his stomach, if he descends from his stomach; after which I make him lie on his back between your hands, and command that he lick his nails as soon as they are repaired, and pull them off at your hands, and sign with your finger the closing of the rupture on the bone of the affected hand, and in a sign that is similar to half of a circle around the circumference of the wound; then wash the cauterization of this form:
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles.	As long as it is white and glistening.
Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui I cussin et I serjant sus les cuisses, et I autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	Then straighten the buns on your leg; and the physician teaches you to mark your hand so that they do not return; and well work on the thighs with the cauterization, and put a piece of cloth and a bandage on each thigh, and the other on the part that the physician marks; then place the cautery at the sign on all your hand, and hold it correctly and as far as you can reach the bone, and if you do not reach it the first time, then continue another one as long as you approach the bone; and be careful not to let the blister come out when you make the cauterization, not to burn it; and so that the physician does not die, or another.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien.	And you should know that when you do not come to the bone at the cauterization, your efforts are in vain.
Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés III jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides XL jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	And it is necessary that the cauterization of children be subtle according to the size of the bone, and the same for adults; after three days, treat the wound of the cauterization with a piece of burre as long as the burn is ostee; after treating other injuries as long as they are healthy, and gently apply 40 jors on his back until the wound is well sore; and it is necessary that the scars be kept far apart, so that the dung does not come out when he gets up from bed.
Et aprés XL jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse XL autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement.	After 40 days, when he wishes to rise, he will find a well-made bandage, and another 40 days later; then he should rest, so that he can work quickly and not have too much overfilling of drink and mud, and not have too high braiding; and when he teaches this lesson, it is completely healthy.
Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And I will say this after the cutting in his chapter.
de la routure dou ventre	of the rupture of the stomach
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai I cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a III angles selonc ceste forme:	When ruptures occur in other stomachs and are known, and you see that they are not increasing, then you should cauterize again according to the quantity, and it is the third part of the keur; after the cure according to what we have said; and no ancient has said that it should be cauterized at the cautery of three angles according to this form:
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile.	The shoulder is lifted and a line is made for the width of the fracture, and another one is made, and both hands are placed on all the cauterization clamps.
Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	The first cauterizations are more gentle and less painful.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	There is no pain in any part of the body.
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor.	When pain comes to any part of the body, either from chill or wound, and the pain lasts long, and medicine does not help, then it is necessary to cauterize at the cauterization point called "points", and the cauterization should be according to the length of the limb, the size, the strength, the location of torsions and the pain.
s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence I autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	If the first fire cautery is healthy, it's well; if not, restart another cautery on the other part, because it is customary to die in the member that is affected, since it must be cauterized as long as the patient remains healthy.
de meselerie	of misery
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie.	The pain is helped once by cauterization, and at the same time the disease that comes from the putrefaction of flesh and melancholy.
Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai V cauteres sus lou chief: I emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et II sus les II cornes, et I derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	Can you see the cauterization, if the disease is at its beginning, and if it is cured according to what we said in the division, and neither delays nor tires, and you doubt that corruption will spoil all the patient, therefore I make you this cauterization: I cut off the head, and the other on the front near the end of the hair; and I touch the horns, and the back of the tail at the end of the hair; and it lasts as much as your hand that the cauterization burns to the bone, and as much as the pus comes out so that the vapors of the large humors may come out; and you cauterize the mouth according to what is in front.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et I cautere en som lou neis, et II cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et VI cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et I grant sus la crupie et I autre delez, et II sus les II espaules; et II sus les coutes, et II sus les tendrons dou pis, et I sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et I autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et I autre sus lou foie.	1. If the burn is widespread; it is clear that if you cauterize with these cauterizations we have mentioned or chief, and the cauterization is in one place, and the cauterizations on the spine of the neck, and the cauterizations on the spine of the back, and the hip and the other groin, and the shoulders and the other elbows, and the wrists and the other ankles, and all the joints of the hands and feet, and the fissures of the hands; and you will have nerves that are burned but not destroyed, which you must not burn; and never made a cauterization on the bone of the elbow, and the other on the stomach, and the other on the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus.	When you perform more cauterizations, the patient benefits more and does not feel pain in cauterization as much as the healthy one because the body is already corrupted to some extent.
Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers.	It is necessary that the cauterization be large and small according to the limbs and joints, according to what you will find in the ways of iron.
Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	After treating the patient with flour several times with honey and other remedies as long as he is healthy.
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the wound comes out in any member and is treated with medicines and oils and plasters, and it is not healthy, then a cauterization is made on the member according to its size and smallness of the member; and if the cauterization is entered into at the edge of the skin; then the treatment of ointments as long as it is healthy.
Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	And no time is made when cauterizing and at the hand, wrist, and back, where the skin is silent and the member is tight; and if it does not swell, none enters unless one knows the members and the courses of the moving nerves of the body.
de albaras	of barbs
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the disease called "albaras" is awakened, and the art of medicine does not help, then cauterize with a cautery piece according to the quantity of the heat, as long as the wound is tight and red, and of the same color; then use flour and lentils with olive oil and plantain leaves, and salt and alum, of each part; and mix all together, and wrap with a cloth, and apply to the skin as much as it needs.
li cure de chancre par cautere	The treatment of syphilis by cauterization
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble I cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.	When the sore appears at the beginning, and you see it stop, if the cauterization is done on the cauterizer who seems to be a circle, all around the circumference of the sore.
Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	And the wise ones say that cauterization is done in the environment of the sore; and it seems to me that this is not good, because I fear that it may become ulcerated and corrupted, and I have never wanted it to happen once; and the most correct thing is that it should be cauterized all around, at the cauterizer called "circle", if as we have said in the mouth of cauterization.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	of the flesh that cannot be measured
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi.	When someone has a disease called 'adubelati', and it delays in measuring either due to excessive production or because the patient is too weak (that is, too old) and has little strength, or due to tightness; and you see it suffering from this: therefore, use the cauterization by inserting small cauterizing points as you prick; afterwards, let it heal.
Car elle se hastera de meureir.	For it will delay in measuring.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you see it perceived at all the cauterization, if the cauterization is hot, then it is not in its proper form.
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis.	And place your hand in the environment of this disease called "adubelati" as long as the burn is perceived by the skin, and be such burns that the patient feels them in a way that the course of the pores is closed to some extent.
Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	After the treatment when it is perfectly healthy.
li cure dou feu par fer	the cure by fire with iron.
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches.	Another kind of disease called "corrodens" and is nothing more than a rot of the member, for it eats away at the members as it does with dry wood.
Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit.	If you see this disease in the shoulder that can suffer a burn at once by fire, then wash the cauteries with small and large stones according to where the disease is; after all are cauterized as much as possible, and nothing remains of it, that all that is corrupted is destroyed.
Et puis le laisse III jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption.	Then let it lie for three days, and put on the burned parts with oil until the caustic wounds are burnt and all the corruption is destroyed.
Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.	After the care of the ignited parts that generate fire.
Et se tu vois aprés III jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus.	If after three days no healthy fire is born, it is good; and if not, continue the cauterization on the parts that are most corrupted.
Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	And this is never cured by medicine in the part of cauterization with fire; but all cauterization with fire is greater help, and I have already said the cure of the ague medicine in the division: take what you have skill in.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	Of the porings that come to the feet
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet.	Many times it happened that the feet were infected with a disease called "closed" according to our understanding, and it is a large thing that has to be done to heal the foot.
Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc II manieres.	And the treatment of this disease is done in two ways.
C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude.	It is to know that it is either burn cauterization or hot water cauterization.
Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe I cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi III jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines.	Burn cauterization if you are hot and hot water cauterization is similar to a pin of vulture, and is made of iron according to the size that can reach the knot of all parts, and has subtle margins; after it is put on all around the knot, and turn your hand totally over the knot as much as it comes to the end of the knot; and it leaves for three days until it begins to secrete milk; then I make an ointment of well-boiled maggots with a cloth, and leave the ointment on all night, and the knot will be loosened from its roots.
Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then, treat the wound with ointment, applying it as soon as it is healthy.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines.	If the wound becomes infected many times, and in the hands and fingers, then it may be necessary to perform a hot iron cauterization. This is done as follows: take a piece of iron or steel, or a needle of gut, and place it on the nail and the hoof, knowing how to pierce warts; then place the iron on so that it burns everything around, then put a little hot water, and hold your hand well, and press your hand as you turn until the edge of the iron touches the root of the nail, and you will find the hot water way perfectly fitted at the root; then allow the malaides a little mordication of the hot water for an hour; then leave it, and it will fall off all its roots.
Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	In this next step, I will create another action, as long as you are aware of all these things that are in the course, then I will treat the wounds that have been inflicted with sharp objects.
li cure dou trembler	I will treat him so he does not tremble.
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices IIII cauteres ou IV sus l’espinee dou dos, I cautere entre chescune espinee; et I cautere ou pez, et I sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	If he trembles from cold, or fever, or other causes, and you must make four cauterizations or four on the spine, one between each spine; and one on the stomach with olive oil cautery; if he continues to tremble, and soon regains his health from the cold disease.
des pustules puans	from pimples that have come out.
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues.	There is no instance where the corpse appears to have bats or pustules that come from large corrupted materials.
si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire.	If it is necessary to cauterize at the first appearance that the pustule seems to have grown, a subtle cautery of mirror's pitch or of the point that is held by fire, or of the cautery of aristolochia root far, or in the lenticular cautery.
Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	And never is the cauterization done at the beginning when they appear in this manner, and it does not grow new questions ahead, but it is disrupted by the superfluity that comes, and they are healed; but it must be done after the evacuation of blood.
quant li artere est copee	When the artery is seized
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	Many times there are large hemorrhages of blood from the artery that is seized at the wound that comes to the pardefuers, or at the incision of the abscess, or at the fire cautery of the member, and similar things; and it is a very serious matter to enrich.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren I, ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	And always when there is none, if you have to put your index finger on the wound of the vein, and hold it as much as possible until it is calmed down by your thumb, and no more pain; then put the olive oil cautery on more or less as many as they are all red; then I, or according to the size of the wound and how it is placed, put it on the vein or where you hold your finger, and hold the cautery on that until it is no longer painful.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement I autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	If it happens while you are tying the shoelace of your child's vein, and the cauterization ends, then quickly take another one from the fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des IIII manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And continue to do this one after another until the nerve is not inflamed, and no other harm comes to the patient; and be careful that when the artery is not cut, it does not cause immediate pain when the artery becomes large, if it is not through one of the four methods we have mentioned: either by cauterization or extraction if it is properly treated, or by gentle pulling with thread, or by medicines placed on it that can cause pain; and be sure to tie and extract it carefully.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Whoever will be in charge of tightly binding wounds with cloths or other similar things, should not profit from it without doing so.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if there is no remedy or medicine present, then he should put his index finger on the wound of the vein as we have said, and firmly press until it is painful from the wound and the vein; and he should not move much, but his hand should be cold often, so that it does not freeze and become numb and painful; and he should apply remedies before those of cauterization and medicines.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	Here comes the first sentence to translate:
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	1. We have told you in the first chapter of all diseases that require cauterization, either with fire or burning medicines, and their causes, effects, and forms of cauterizations; and I put this chapter of the chief's own writing, and I will go to this chapter by my own way because it is lighter to go there.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	2. But if you begin this, it is necessary, as you say, that you learn that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than in the first cauterizations, and for this reason greater caution is required.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	3. For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie.	I advise you not to attempt foolishness.
Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures.	For people have many ways of treating.
si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	If they come from those who have died so easily due to their disease, and the severity of their evil; and these are the ones we should fear.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse.	And those who say to you: "Wait, I am in pain"; and the disease is despicable.

It only requires you to allow those who come to you to have this manner, but put more caution in your honor than in your covetousness, and do not give way too easily but wisely of what you are certain, and what you can take and lose; and use prognosis and indication in the cures of your maladies as for salus so converted; and this will help you to this good reputation, glory, and memory of longing.

Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	I have commanded this chapter in designing it according to the rules of cauterization, as I have designed the rules of cauterizations from the chief joints, because you will find it more easily what you will have to do.
dou chief plein d’aigue	A full-sized chief with sharp edges.
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	Saiges that this disease comes from the mother many times in childbirth, and when the head is pulled too hard from the child's head; and never has it come from any other cause that it is known.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And I have never seen this disease as an infant, and in these cases the death followed quickly; and for this it seems to me that I should divide the work among different treatments.
Et je vis I enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com II nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	And I have seen children with acute diarrhea, and the chest swelled each day until it could not sustain itself; and he believed so much that it was death, and this moisture is assembled between the ribs and the skull, from the knee to the skull; and the ovary is such when the moisture is between the knee and the skull, and the abscesses are small, which you can treat with a large incision in the chest; and so long as the moisture increases, the form of the spatulation:
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai II fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is more intense, and the abscess is larger, then I make incisions in the manner of a cross, according to this form:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief III fendures selonc ceste maniere:	And if the moisture has made the bone soft, and you see the commissures of each part are overstretched, and the wound gushes out when you press with your hand on the denuded area, and this is not unusual: then it may be that you cut off the head III times according to this manner:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers.	And after the incision, remove all the moisture.

After extracting the thistles and powders, and pour in wine and oil, and let it remain for five days; then remove it, and treat the wound with plasters and poultices, and let the head be evenly pressed, and then massage the dry cheese-like meat as much as the member is comfortable and healthy.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	Another way to make an incision is to look at or open the large end of the abscess, and the sharp edge; for it is never beforehand, never behind, never to the side, and never to the bottom.

Therefore, the size of the opening should be according to what you have; and make sure not to block the artery; and come down with the blood, if the patient dies from the blood and the evacuation of pus.

des larmes	of tears

The text describes the process of treating a temporal bone fracture on the left side of the head, making an incision into the bone; removing the hand from the nerves of the temples that move in the mastectomy; when the bone is exposed, if all the blood comes out onto a sponge, then place between the two lips of the incision and put cotton on it, and sew with linen; then cover the rough edges with moistened vinegar and oil, and keep away from infection; when it is healed, if you rub the bone until it charred and began to rust, then the treatment of things that cause excision, which make the char.

de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the ear's sweat
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des IIII choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	All that comes out of the ears is one of the four things: grains, or fat, or mine pit or similar thing as if it were made of iron; or seed, like beans, peas, or peas; or something that flows, like phlegm and pus and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	When it comes out of the ear pit or in any other way than what sticks to the ear, and does not grow in the ear, put the ear to the sun.

If you see the piercing, and it does not distill any drop of violet oil or marrow oil, then extract it; and I make the congestion disappear, and it snores when it exhales, and put in the ear pieces of linen or wool; and the ear is at ease.
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	This treatment often comes out; and if it does not come out, then extract it with fine tweezers, as follows is the form:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it jumps out with tweezers, it is good; if not, then extract it with a fine hook and double needle; and if it does not jump out, then make a small cut in the ear and pull the tip of the ear or the canal; and sniff the part that enters the ear with wax if it comes without entering with the ear, then form it as we have said; and if it does not come out in this way, then take some cotton and insert it; then press the wax on the piercing or whatever it is, and extract it.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	1. If she does not jump from all these things that we have said, if you persist in hurting her ear despite the chalk and vein spasm; and the way of hurting it is to first clean the male patient's head with the mouth of the helmet, according to the measure of its strength, then hold the patient's head between your hands and turn the ear towards the opposite side, and make a small cut at the root of the ear in the fat or depending on the ear; and the cut should be like a moon, as you move towards the piercing, then the bone according to your power, and the saliva runs to your mouth; and the cure as soon as it is healthy.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre I spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if it is grainy and it swells, then apply the extraction; and if it cannot be extracted, then apply the spumous substance according to this form.
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	and apply an incision to that grain.

s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	If it jumps for this, that's good.

de l’estoupement des oreilles	Of the cold of the ears
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient I poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born without having a cold in the ears; and this very thing happens due to a cold in the chest or an earache, and there is no sign of any discharge from the ear, unless one can see; and never has there been a puff of snot, and it is well seen.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	That which comes out is of grief in the healing in more positions, and in this case it is necessary to put the ear with cold in the sun; and look at: if you see the exudation apparent, then the ear has completely formed this salty substance.
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And so, and also, shave all the hair from the head, if it does not hurt the ear; if the exfoliation is of a thin layer or a curl of the ear, if the hands are gently pinched, and the cup lightly, as long as that layer is entirely removed.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	And if the exfoliation is complete in the ear, if I take a gentle razor and scrape a little with fire, then he puts or curl of the ear.

If you feel the exfoliation that the patient feels pain in the ear, gently pinch it, and keep your fingers off the ear; then put in the ear a tent according to the large part of the pustule, and apply Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	1. Then apply the cure once it is clean and dry.

If the wound continues to bleed, then dip a sponge in cold water and wrap it around the ear, and place it on the ear, and use other remedies that stop the flow of blood that are treated with distillations.
de la char des papieres	Of the book of papers
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	That is the best way to treat wet hairs that come from papers when they are dry and then, if you extend them with needles and tweezers, and place them on a piece of glass with its roots; then put the lew in vitrol.

de la gresle	The first sentence to translate is: "Ou cautere
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	The first sentence to translate is: "Ou cautere
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	The first sentence to translate is: "Car en l'ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l'incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	1. If the snow is descending towards the earhole towards the part of the ear, and if you reverse the paper, and the snow is held with tweezers, and the paper is pressed from both sides; and if the paper is moved away by incision, it causes no harm; and when the snow is applied, if you lift the oil of bitter salt, and cure the ear from which char is formed as much as the malady allows.
de la graisse des eulz	1. of the grease of the hairs
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	1. Exinach is a grease that is engrained in the papers of the children, and this happens more as time passes, and it causes pain to their hairs, and they come to the catharsis in the mornings, and cannot see the light of the sun because their tears are on their hairs; and for this they lie down with their faces covered, and sleep, and their papers become wet with the exinach that oozes from the oil.
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press on your knee and feel the excruciating pain inside.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren I drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And the manner of the incision if it is that the barber sets his finger in your mouth; then take a piece of linen and make a circle according to the quantity of pain contained in each part, then put it on his finger; and press with both hands on one side and the other, so that the pain is assembled within the circle; then make a cut in the moisture at the corner of the nail, no larger than the wound you make in the gum of the mouth; and make the cut as long as you see the pain; and in other positions, the pain comes from the cut, according to the form of a piece of greasy white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	1. "Tear the cloth into pieces all of them between your two arms at the deflowering, and turn your hands to the right and left as much as possible; and make sure you do not push in the fleece, that you do not get to the whole satin roll, that you do not bleed.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	2. Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then the doctor, when he is healthy.
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the abscess comes to the head, then the doctor should apply dressings that are soft and healthy as much as possible.
des poilz des papieres	of the papers' hairs.
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc IIII manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When papers are born with hairs other than their nature, and they are dried out, if they harm the hairs, and bring about diseases such as tears and mucus from papers and albugine, until it is caused by the destruction of the hairs; and the cure is done in four ways: either by burning together with fire, or by medicine according to what is before or in the chapter of cauterization, and it is made by incision and stitching or by needles, according to what I will say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai I fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai I fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	1. and if not, then leave the stitch and the threads as they are for three or four days; then cure the wound with the stitch and the threads that are dry and constricting, because the paper relieves the wound and its assembly, but the stitch is dead (as they say the ancient ones), and it is over for pain; and if in another way: and it is that you see the paper of a figure that is as well-made as the fur of the marten, as we have seen, at three incisions it will follow the form that is here:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	Then comes the one who surpasses with small forces according to the form that is here:

Then comes the one who surpasses with small forces according to the form that is here: If you cannot hold the nails, and the thing is not equal, then take a needle or if it has one thread, and pull out the fil; and take another thread of the great larmier, and the small thread of the little, and assemble the threads evenly between your two hands; then gently lift your hand evenly, and gently sew all the edges where you have signed, as we have experienced, then assemble the two lips of the wound by stitching, and cure it as soon as it is healthy; and if the suture comes to your incision, if the pain and swelling ease; and never has there been that the hair of the paper is converted: if you use what we have said about the incision; but the stitching in one and the other is more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai II caines par art, et II liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as II chiés de II pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les II cainnes des II parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui. S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If the patient is delayed and the force is applied, then treat it as soon as it is healthy; and if the wound is sore, and if the paper is lifted, and no hair is tied, and this is the form of the shoulder you will make according to this figure and quantity of long and wide:
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute I fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse I autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a I ou II ou III ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	The first line of the translation is: "The dislocation is such that you need a fine needle, and a piece of silk thread; then assemble the heads and gently pull them apart, and make the ends of the threads as long as possible; then cut off the other fine silk thread, and pull the heads; then put the sutures in your mouth; and if the sun is out, so that the dislocation is visible, because it is a delicate one and small, then cut the needle all through the thread in the root of the hair as far as it grows naturally, and trace it on paper as you pull it out with your natural hair; then pull the hair until it comes out all the way through the thread in the paper, and pull out any hair that is left, if there are one, two, three, or more; then pull your hand as far as the hair comes out all the way through the paper with your natural hair.

de la porriture de l’oil	Of the oil's fat
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	When this disease, called "aleacrati" or oil comes in two ways: naturally, and unnaturally.

de la bowe de l’oil	from the oil of the eye
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit. des aigues de l’oil	of the oil's waters

se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	If the patient becomes agitated now, if they see the surgeon in front of them and the instrument in their hand.

se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	1. de la char sor le neis	of the fire and the needle.
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	No fires or needles are ever born or become different, and if there are any that seem like scorpions at the mouth of the pie; and if they have a fire enhanced with fuchy color, and if they have a fire of good color.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	In that case of these fires which are not enhanced, and do not become enhanced, it is necessary that you place the patient between your hands before the sun; and operate on their noses, and wet the onions with those fires, and draw them out; so that you may be able to hold them in the subtle substance of a part, as long as you can see that the fire is completely extinguished.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout I des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	If there is nothing else that can be done, if you examine all the surgical instruments lightly and subtly, without causing any harm; and if you do not have an assistant, or if you have to operate alone, and if the wound is malignant, then cauterize as much as possible and burn until the bones are charred and the wounds are all closed, then gargle with warm water and apply an ointment or a poultice.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	If you do not have any moisture, and the wound is dry, then it is healthy; and if the wound is not charred in the bone, then it has not penetrated the bone, and the instruments cannot be trimmed: therefore, it is necessary to tie a knot with a piece of linen as large as possible, and use your hands, and place one between each tooth or less; and put the end of the thread in the child's mouth as soon as it comes out of the gum, and carry it around until it comes out of the mouth; and often do this for the child in schools, and it is a light thing for those who see it; then hold the chief that comes through the nose with one hand, and the other chief that comes through the mouth with the other hand, and follow it after the other until it is all done.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	1. Until you know that the child has corrupted the char, take the child's penis, clean it, and wipe it with Egyptian ointment, and then put it back in the urethra as before; do this 3 times or more, until the ointment corrodes all that is left of the char; then put a catheter of plastic for some days until it is healthy, and if you have knowledge of dried herbs, use them; and this is the form of the instrument to purify the child's penis, or when distilled oils and medicines are needed.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	2. And it should be of silver or gold, resembling a hanging lamp, like a leash, and it is led thus; and if you see, if a leash is closed, and the purging fluids reach the child's penis, and there is one hand on the penis to hold it while heating the oil or no liquid.
de la char sor le neis	Of the char of the knee
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Many times it happens at the head of the knee a disease called "telul", which grows and becomes large, so that it is a sight to behold; therefore it is necessary to cut it off at the beginning, and then remove the bone entirely, and then put on the fire cautery or hot medicine; and if it is delayed as long as it is large, if it is hard, of dark color, poor sensation: if it does not touch iron at all because it is enchanted, for when one cuts it once, no harm comes to the patient; and if the enchantments are many, not of dark color, and you see that it can be covered, if the patient is open and the mouth is closed, and cure the leu of things loose and restricting.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	When the wound is cleaned and dressed
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	When it comes to the continuation of treatment, one of these cartilages is inserted, and does not last long, for no one.

It is necessary therefore to do this if no one comes to help, and if the wound is fresh at all points; and then apply a bandage, and treat it until it heals; and if the lips are already sunken on both sides, it is necessary to scrape off all the parts that are healthy, and then assemble the lips in a bandage, and extract them, and sprinkle them with dragon's blood powder, and incense burnt; and put a piece of a plaster soaked in other ointment on the powder, and leave it until it dries, and treat the ointment as necessary.

des apostemes des levres	of lip tumors
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	The lips of the tumors are hard and resemble grains of wheat, becoming smaller and larger; therefore, it is necessary to cut off the lips, and each time you cut, take them with tweezers and pull out in each part; then use the blade after cutting the vitreol broits, as long as they are not bleeding; and then the blade of the scissors, and cure the blade of dry things as long as it is healthy.
de la char des gencives	Of the horse's knee

des sordens	of the sutures

Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary when you treat the patient's tooth pain that you wait as long as possible and then eat, because it should not be done; for it is a substance of high value, therefore there is no excuse to neglect it.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	When the patient is forced to eat, if you are certain that the tooth will not hurt.

Many times the pain of the patient's tooth has passed, and make sure that the tooth is clean, and give it to chew the tooth; and if you are certain that the pain will not return as long as the mouth is dry, because we have already wanted to do this for these healthier ones; and when you are sure that the tooth is well cleaned, then scrape the tooth with a spatula hard enough to protect the gums of all parts; then the mouth should have your needles well inserted in the first place and then insert them more deeply, until they are well fixed, then affirm the needles; and make sure that the patient's tooth is in your healthy bone between your teeth, and hold it well so that it does not move.
