If the teeth are felt and gnawed, then it is necessary to fill them with cloth, whether they are loose or not; and if the tooth is gently twisted with pins, it will not break in the pulling; and it is wise to overturn the girdle to clean the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And be well aware that you will not break it, and there will remain a part, and the patient suffers from the malice of the root, greater pains in the first.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	1. And you should not make a wound like the ignorant healers who, with their haste and their hardiness, break the charm never, and do not harm anyone that we have known; but they bring it once by the agony of this great disease, either by the roots that they cut, or by the charm that they break, as often as we want; and when it is raw, wash the limb with wine or vinegar and salt; and if they come out with blood, which often happens, use the limb with vitriol; and if it does not work, cauterize.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The shapes of the teeth, whether they are at the front or back, are long and wide, and do not double in size when you pull the tooth; these are the shapes:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And they should be of large bones if they do not break when pulled, and they should be made of good iron, and they should have sharp points to hold onto.
de la racine des dens	of the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root of the tooth is dry when pulled, if it comes to pass that you must cut into the gum with a sharp knife, then:
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	as long as the root is smoothed, then cut off the points that are called "algorif" (a type of tooth), even if the gums look like a beard; and they should be made in the same way as a lime and this is the shape:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out of all these nails, then you must pull the handle as far as the root, and then put the instrument called "athali", which is a pincer, in the form of:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And if it is very large and does not break the bone, and if the root jumps from this, it is good; if not, then help yourself with all the tools, and follow these forms that come after:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait II rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you help yourself with this instrument that has two rings, then the form is:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other instruments that are in front in the reason of the teeth, and this instrument which seems large nails, then the form is:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	1. And so it should be that it cannot break, and it should be sharp like the ends of bones; and also other fragments, which are not least; and the surgeons use their own instruments subtly, according to what their hands and the disease demonstrate, because they have some diseases or the ancients did not teach any instrument for the diversity of bones, and it does not break at the wrong place or other bones, or it causes harm, if it seeks out fragments that I have said, and helps with gestures, according to the form.
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	2. And let it be thick and well-held to hold the bone, so that it does not slip, but can hold and oster; and then restore the leu of medicines corresponding to this, and if there is any porriture in the bone, and it is small, if all this instrument is used:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the tooth appears that does not fit with the natural corporeal form, and its shape is unpleasing, and even more so in women, it comes to pass that you must cut off the tooth after the tooth has erupted, and it is not straight, and it cannot be smoothed or filled: therefore, the gum; and if it is erupted with the tooth, then take this instrument whose form is like the small tooth, and it should be of hard metal, and be sharp and pointed.
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the cut is quickly and quickly in the hands with the hard tooth, and because you do not move the others, and if it appears that it can be filled, then you can fill it with a piece of gum like this form.
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	1. And it comes as if the lime is made like the eagle's claw; and in the lime the tooth is rarely and lightly placed in the hands, so that it does not move until it chisels; then the edge at the end has no roughness, and the tongue bends too much and breaks the language, if it can mold the spicier as much as it can be even, so that it does not break the tongue or corrupt the speech.
quant li dent lochent	2. When the tooth is placed.
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	3. When the tooth is placed by pressure or by blows, and the patient cannot press on it because of the pain, and you cure them with restraining medicines, and it does not work; if they are to be restrained by a golden thread, because the silver threads turn green and rot, but the gold does not stay; and if the thread is too thick or too thin, according to the quantity of spice between the teeth; and if you see the teeth, take the thread and double it between the two healthy teeth, then place the heads between the bad teeth, as long as you see understanding in the healthy tooth on the other part; then continue the covering where you began, and gently and wisely move your hand, so that it does not move at all; and if your finger is at the root of the tooth, so that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Then the patient should fix the string to the head of the tooth, assemble it, and then place it between the healthy teeth, and put it in so that it does not break the tongue; and then leave it as tight as possible, and if it slips, or the thread comes off, if it is tightened by another thread; if it stays and serves for all its tension, and this is the shape of the teeth and the figure of the second healthy teeth and the second gums, as you see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth is loose, if it is reset in its place, tighten it gradually, as we have said; and do not let it stay in place if it is not firm and painful, and never make it like a bone of a mare's tooth, and put it on where it was lost, and tighten it as we have said, and it lasts and serves for all its tension.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	The first sentence to translate is: "de coper lou liein de la lengue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	No time is there a tongue that comes out of the mouth or nature, which is not caused by an accidental wound; or if it is caused by a wound, and the mouth is so deep that it reaches the madman's mouth, and it is made to laugh with its own hand, then it is the nervous one that is most large, as long as the tongue is dislodged from its place, and if it is sharp or out, and it is a painful wound, if it pierces the uncinate and the large one immediately follows; and keep in mind that the fever should not be too much, for the artery is out of place; and when you have done this, if the tongue is red and sore, or cold, then put the tongue between two linen sheets; and the madman will be touched every night, that the one who uses it can be soothed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	And if the wound becomes infected, if it is not treated immediately with vitrelle broth; and if it is left untreated, then the cauterization on the slow-healing cautery, which is applied at the base of the wound, must be performed as soon as possible; then the care for another treatment until it is healed.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see the wound to be red or black or hard, and the patient does not feel it, if it is not touched, because it is a gangrene; and if it is inclined towards the blenchor, and it has moisture, if it oozes pus, and the smell of a subtle spumous liquid, and the delivery of a part and another; and if the patient is left untreated in your care, then apply vitrelle broth as soon as possible, until all the wound is dressed; then lift the limb from the wound and the care for other treatments until it is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	of abscesses of the chin
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	Never has a gangrene of the chin appeared that is called "godath," and they are properly called the second mandibles, and when you treat them, as we have said in the division, and they are not healthy, then keep guard: if they are abscesses of small sense and flesh color, and not touching much iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if it is red and the root is thick, and not touching much iron, then not to touch it for the evacuation of blood; but let it remain as long as it is dead, and then you will take it out, or it will split by itself; and if it is pustular color and the root is subtle, and you have prepared the instrument for covering, but first look to see if the abscesses of the chin are resting and are calmed.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Then I make the patient face the sun, and their head is in good condition, and they open their mouth and the tongue is placed between their hands, and they press the entire instrument against the lingua, whatever it may be, whether silver or gold: and it is as fine as some nails.
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	Do you press the tongue against all this instrument, and see the incision, if you take the pincers and the needle in the hare, and draw it as far as you can; and take no other thing with you, then the cop is made of the instrument, whatever may be its form, which seems like some forces; and the whole of it is corbeled, and one part turns into another, and are very crooked, and is made of iron or steel:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument present, if you lack needles, then the form is like this:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	And let it be divided on one side and named on the other; and when you cut an eggplant, if you cut the other according to the same manner, and after the incision, apply warm, hot water to the patient's face, and make it cool, and if blood comes out, if the hot water is applied, or burns from pomegranate seeds are cooked, or from mustard, and similar things, until the mouth is not sore; then the cure is as long as it is healthy; and never do other abscesses appear in the mouth than the two eggplants, if they are cut as the two eggplants are cut.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And I treated a woman with a small abscess in her throat, which was causing difficulty swallowing; she had closed most of the gullet, so the woman could not breathe through the blocked duct, and could neither drink nor eat, and died if she delayed for one or two days.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	The abscess was so large that it had required two incisions through the two holes.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	I then removed the entire piece of bone, and took out a large portion of the intestines; I then removed another piece from the other hole, and closed the mouth and pressed on the tongue; after removing the bone from these abscesses and taking out a part, there was only a little pus left; and then she was able to swallow again, and began to drink water and wine, and continued to cut down on this abscess with long strokes; the abscess grew larger and filled the socket that I had made, so that it would not fit in; therefore I removed and cauterized the abscess: afterwards she improved; and I left these parts, and only God could do more for her after me.
de l’uve	The first line of the text is "de l
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When the head of the urethra is drawn downwards, and it is long and thin, it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is very large and bent, it is called "urethra".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	If it is treated as we have described in the division, and the cure does not benefit, and you see that the wound is calmed and made small, then it is appropriate to touch it; and the one that is bent and is not long can be assembled; and if it is bloodstained or has a strange color or black, then it is appropriate to avoid cutting into it.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great risk to the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	It is therefore necessary, when you see, according to the method I have described, that the patient's gallbladder and length are considered, that you place the patient facing the sun, and press the lower lip on the instrument we made note of earlier; then clean the eye with the water, and pull it out, and the copper is in the two segments I mentioned in the incision of the two breasts.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And it is necessary that you do not copper more than the superfluity that is over the natural end; for if you cope more, you will grieve the voice and speech; and after the incision, use what we said in the incision of the two breasts, and cure as long as it is healthy.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient is afraid of pain, then you must use an engine for the fire cautery of the other pain.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the manner of cauterization is sharp and quick.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And the patient puts his head on your hand, and then presses his tongue onto the instrument we mentioned in the chapter of cauterization, and confines with sharp, live fire, so that it is not too thick or too clear; and with this use of the instrument's edge, the form is:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient has a hair or puts medicine on his cheek, like the cat's tail, and places the instrument in all the medicine on the eye; and the patient is anxious on his side, if the saliva and the mucus flow from his mouth of the medicine given, if it does not descend to the throat and the chin, then hold your hand on all the medicine and press on the eye, the half of an hour, as long as you see that the pain and the medicine's bitterness are calmed; and if you see, take cotton and wrap it around any instrument, and wet the cotton in the medicine, and withdraw the instrument from the cotton into the case of the cord, as long as the cotton dries on the eye; and do this often, as long as the cauterization is perfect, then let it dry, and after four or five hours, if you have skill in re-cauterizing the medicine, if it resumes, and after the cauterization of the excrement into the eye, wrap it in cotton and put it in a bottle, and clean what is outside of the medicine; and be washed with cold water, and be cured with gargles as long as it is healthy.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is safer than incision alone; if it is treated with fumigation according to this method, take calamine, iodine, oregano, rosemary, chamomile, and any other herbs, and mix them all together or any of them in one pot, and add water, and boil; and it can be well glued with strong earth, and the pot should have the instrument made according to this method:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	And it should be of silver or gold, and one of the ends of the shoulder is put in the patient's mouth as much as the vapor rises through the nose, until the nose is numb; after that it often resumes, until the nose is dry, and keep that you do not make this at the beginning of the onset of gangrene, because many things come; and do not make this unless the decline of gangrene has begun.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And if this instrument is not present, then take a needle and put some wax on the tip of the needle, if the mouth of the patient has not been too dry; for the wax on the needle does not grease the mouth, and it is good for the overall cure.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times it has happened in the throat, either with a bone or a fish spine, or nothing at all; if it comes to that, then you must see what you can, and press the tongue against the sun with all the instrument, so that you can see the thing; and if it does not open and is pinned in the throat, it is necessary to make the patient vomit unless the meat is cooked in the stomach; by chance, if it is moved by vomiting; or if the patient swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of navel, or a root of lettuce, or a morsel of dry bread; and then press it on the sponge, and then glutenize it; and when it reaches the stomach, if it is not, and then draw it back; and if it does not come back from what we have said, then take the instrument of plucking according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	1. And let the strap be placed around the neck if it can more gently enter the mouth, and raise the head; and guard that you do not touch the epigastrium, that all may survive, and do not force the bones; and it is best that the patient and the instrument force the tool, because it is best or the thing is there; if it is forced, or it is drawn further along all the instrument evenly, as far as it can be.
de la sansue de la gorge	2. of the throat's slackness
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	3. No time is medicine useless, as I said in the division, by the cure of medicines; and when it does not profit, then look at the mouth of the patient in the sun, then that you press the tongue to the instrument that I have told you.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	If you see the joint, if it is all small and sharp-edged, or if it has fine points like this one.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	If it is not worth anything, if you take a hair, and pull on the patient's throat with the hair, then pull or cut the hair as needed, and do this often.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And the patient's neck is always sweating.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	Then take full advantage of the cool sweat on your neck, and open your mouth, and you feel that it is swallowing, and move it with your hand often; and if the joint still feels hot, then it is not worth anything.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	If she does not understand as we have said, if the patient smokes tobacco, use the instrument I mentioned in the fumigation of the eye; do this many times, as it will cause discomfort.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And the manner of the fumigation if you prefer to use either tobacco or charcoal, and place the cover over a covering in the environment, and in the other part, place the head of the instrument; then perform your fumigation, and the patient places the end of the cord in his mouth, closes his mouth, so that the smoke does not enter, but goes to the throat; and the throat will now hurt, and if it restarts the fumigation many times; and suffer the patient's thirst, and drink salty and acidic things, and do not drink lemon water; and then perform the task that was intended by this government.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the form of the instrument used to treat the wound, if it is, when it can be seen, resembles tines like corbels to enter the mouth; it has the appearance of a surgeon's beak, and has sharpness like lime, so that whatever it takes, it cannot hold onto it; and thus the form is:
li chapistres des apostemes	The procedures for the abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	The appearances of the abscesses are, according to what is remembered in this book, and they vary in puncture and size; and there are two ways in which one is in its own appearance itself, and due to it being moist.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second method if by the hands or they are in the course.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	Because the apostes of the head are different from those of the foundation, and the apostes of the lower limbs are different from those that come in joints, and each has its own judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	And if an apostem is not properly felt, as long as the bow is dead according to its completion; and if there are such cases where it is necessary to feel when they are believed, and they do not die according to their completion, like those of joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when apostes come from dead joints, and they are left as long as they are porous, by chance if the ligament and nerve of the joint are corrupted, because this is due to contraction in that member.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	For the incision, if it is of the principal member, and you delay the piercing as long as possible before it becomes mortal, it will harm the principal member; or it is of the foundation, if the hole is not made quickly before it becomes mortal, it will harm the foundation. And only that the incision believes to have completed digestion, rather than the one that is of the foundation, it will not cause mortality, and it will be long-lasting and form a fistula; and it cannot heal in a great time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And it is necessary that you clean the wound of the incision of the member that is mortal according to the completion, and when the pain is calmed, when the fever subsides, when the pain and the bruising are eased, and the debate and the ague of the wound of the incision, and the other signs; and it is necessary that you sew the wound or more dependent on the member of the incision, and where it has been opened; and it should be the wound long and of great length, and if the wound is in the hands or feet, or in joints and in the nerves and arteries, and in all of them equal or without soreness.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In those that prick, according to the member.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when an abscess is in the body, if it is confirmed that you leave the puncture until it is completed in digestion, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	For if you prick before it, if it is long in coming from him, and it pains the belly; and by chance they harden the lips and become flattened from it.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if there is no abscess that is known by the wide belly, according to which member it belongs.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	And it is necessary that you cut out small abscesses, small pustules; and in large abscesses, large pustules, and many fangs according to the appearance of the abscess; and if in such abscesses or they have to be cut off the head, and closed; when it becomes as hard as I am, and is dried, then it must be done as with bubbles: and if in such cases that are cut at three angles, and if in such that are closed like the fang of a snake, as with abscesses of the gout; and if in such that are made with a small cut, and others with different sizes and appearances closed.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	1. Those who have no chief, if the grief is superficial like a wound, it is necessary that you cut it finely; and when the grief is large, and has caused great pain, and you cut it, if you do not stain all the wound with your tool in that hour, but only part of it, then the grief will soon heal to the other side, then you will not touch anything proper; do this many times, as long as the wound is completely healed; at the same time, if the patient is weak in virtue, or a woman carries, or small children, or old men with decayed limbs.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For the expectorants have never been seen with the end of the bowel, which is sometimes lost, and you will not find it.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Avoid this chapter with great caution, and when you have discovered your abscess, if the wound is large, look at the size of the abscess; and if it is a small one, use a linen or cotton bandage; and if it is large, and there are many pustules, then wrap each in a separate bandage so that one may cover the other; and if you have cut into leather a part of the wound, and you have healed it, then fill it with fine cloth or ragging from linen or wool, and sew it to the edge of the wound; then the bone, and the care of the ointment as long as it is healthy.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if the blood comes out of the vein when you open it, if it is cold and wet, and thin, and many drops come out, and you put the leu in the dislocation many times.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the blood comes out of the vein when you open it, if it is cold and wet, and thin, and many drops come out, and you put the leu in the dislocation many times. And if the wound is deep and painful, and the pustules that I mentioned in my hands are in this book, and if you have dressings and ointments to relieve the pain, and you apply them to the wound and the pustules, and if the wound is charnus, and the pustules are wet or oily, or in wine and oil, just as we said, then close the wound and the pustules and the dressings, as necessary, until it is healthy.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And this comes when you completely understand the treatment of abscesses: or if you have asked how to go before the treatment of abscesses, and here is the chapter.
des soros	of blood
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	When the chief comes to treat abscesses, and they are done in the same way as the gallbladder, like the surgeon's knife, and it is made in different ways.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	It can be thick and hard or moist like poultry; and if it is hard and rough to cut, and there is no doubt that the knife will not do otherwise.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the description of the size if you are able to see with all the instruments called "enterotome", because the form comes after, what it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, they are made longer than necessary.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	And when the moisture is seen, it should not be left with any hair that contains the moisture, because it will return if left alone; then dip cotton in Egyptian linen soap; if present, use African soap and linen; and leave the wound; and whatever is cut should be treated.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then resume the cotton, as before, on the second day, and the wound, as you can see, will not stop hurting; then treat the wound with ointment according to what is convenient, until it is healthy.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	When the patient holds their breath, if the pulse follows this form, it is too long; and the bones of the shoulder girdle are exposed, the skin is burned from all sides, and all care is focused on drawing out the arrow or spear; and if the artery is contraction, I will do as I have said after this.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And if the aposteme is severe, I will cut and clean it as I have described.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	The wound is made around the severe aposteme and is cleaned because there is little blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	If there is no moisture in any of these apostemes or wounds, and they are not from an old woman's needle; and I found the aposteme as a sharp, rough, and bloody pierce, which could not be broken; and if none was made, it would have been as a sharp wound.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	In other cases of the same type or kind, it is better that those who come for the children and the roots of the ears be opened as soon as possible, even if it depends on the most dependent part of the ear; and they are treated according to what is necessary.
des scrophules	of scrofuly
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Often times there are abscesses at the collarbone, and they are opened, and the plates are removed, and the wounds are cleaned, and never have I seen any other part or part that is not sore, and they are sewn together with one another.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	And each case of scrofuly is properly located on the side, as we have said, and the appearances of these scrofuly are many.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	1. It has needles that contain moisture, and if they are from malicious ones who will not obey nature.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	1. In the one that you see in good position at the hem, and resembles the color of the healthy skin, and is silent from every part and not too deep as nerves of the heart or artery, and is not very sharp; if it comes that you cut it with a razor, and burns in every part, and are the lips of the knee as the nails, if you have skill, as we have said in aphorisms of the chief; and it will be short and few, and you will be sure that you do not cut the nerve or vein, and will not be too sharp, that the hands do not slip, and do not see too soon, that you do not cut more than you should.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	And if you prick the vein or artery, and it does not bleed, then put vitriolet powder on the wound, or any other dust that remains salty, and stretch the wound; and leave it until the poultice is saturated, and soothes the wound, and begins to slough.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	And if the wound is not saturated, then return to your vein as soon as you can; then wait for your physician's mark to see if it shows any small scabs, whether they are coming or going.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if the scab is at the root of the wound, then only prick that scab with a double-strong thread, but do not remove it; then apply the wound with soft cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment, then the cure.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	If you cover the entire wound, then assemble the two lips of the wound, and hold it now, before there is any excess due to the size of the wound.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	If you understand how to cover the root of it, and draw it out, and hold it as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those wounds that are swollen, pierce them if they are not closed; and pierce them as in the one mentioned earlier, depending on the size, then apply ointments and similar things until the corruption is cured; and when the wound is healed, if the cure of the ointment is successful, as much as it is healthy.
de squinance	Of the glabella
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancients spoke and talked about the measurement of the throat; but I have never seen anyone in our time who does this, and this is the writing of their speech.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	For those with squinance, it is necessary that the incision of the throat, which is called 'epiglottis', be avoided; and this cannot be helped by it, because all the veins and the pormon of the maimed are in those who have had the mouth chopped off, or in the throat or in the lips.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is in the throat, it is necessary to cut off the epiglottis to avoid the destruction that comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	It is necessary, then, when we wish to cut the epigastrium, that we cut it in three or four circular cuts, each about a quarter of an inch wide, passing through the two circles, and not too deep into the cartilage; and they are easily sectioned from the epigastrium without causing any damage, and the edges are long enough to suture.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	If the master is unable to do it, then it extends the jaw bone all the way to the chin, then cuts through the muscle as far as it goes to the chin; and avoid the arteries of the neck, if you see nothing, and then cut through the fascia, as we have said; and is demonstrated by the section of the raw flesh from the chin that springs from the bone that is broken, and from the lack of voice; and leaves the wound overstretched a piece.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les II levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the hour has passed since the injury, gather the two lips of the wound as much as possible, and press on the entire surface of the cartilage; then administer medicines that make the wound healthy, as soon as it is clean.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasim does not know how to do this until the throat is completely swollen, and the patient is in danger of death, and there is a shortage of thread.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	Therefore, one should act on the epigastrium because the patient cannot breathe, and they respire through the wound, and it is kept alive; and for this reason, the ancients commanded to leave the wound over until the malady had passed, and it had passed in three days or four; and therefore, they commanded to suture the wound and cure it, as soon as it was cured. And I will tell you what I see.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	I see that a maiden is bleeding, and she has cut her throat, and part of her hair is missing; and I was called to cure her, and I found her already dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discover the wound, and I find the blood that issued from it, and although she did not have much vein or lead to the gorge, the wound was caused by the blood.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	I hurried to the wound, and I treated it as soon as she was healed; and she did not return to the maiden until she was silent of voice, and returned after her disposition; therefore, I say that in the cutting of the epigastrium there is no great pain.
de la grosse gorge	Of the large jaw
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	Hernias are called "hernia of the jaw," and are large hernias of a yellowish color, and are more common in women; and they occur in two ways: natural and accidental; or natural has no engine.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And the accident occurs in two ways: one is similar to large muscles, and the other is similar to hernia that comes from the artery; and if it is painful, and does not overcome the force that is small, and the test and search for all the introitus: if you trueve as I am fat, and cannot in any way, if the cope, so as to cut all its cloth, if it has none; and carefully finish it, and cure as much as possible, until it is perfectly healthy.
des nous	The first sentence to translate is
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	There are many ways of us, which I will describe all the appearances; and it is necessary that I tell the difference between birth and issue.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that issue is childbed fever and ague, as long as the fevers have passed and are accompanied by the purge; therefore, the fever and the ague rest.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	With the newborn there is no fever or ague, and contains the sweat, which is its own bag and is according to the color of the forehead, and becomes like a vesicle, and grows; and they are according to two appearances, either rough or moist, and the color is as I said in the division.

It is necessary, when you come to the cure of a newborn, that you examine and first inquire into all the instruments called "entromising," according as their form comes or chapter which follows.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	And the manner of inquiring into the abscesses of the body is that you press or more wetly on the part where the abscess is, and turn your two hands and hands often until you feel that the thrust has entered the cavity, then that is according to the size of the abscess; then draw out the entromising instrument, and hold it steady in the direction of the thrust.

et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet II jors ou III, tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	1. de la routure de l’artere	of the rupture of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans. As for the arteries and veins, when they become inflamed, they come with the nerves when they are too tight or from too much work, and similar things happen.

des grosses boces pendans	large necks hanging
