dou chancre	The first sentence to translate is "dou
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have said in the division of the appearances of a gumma, and it is commented that one must oversee by medicines, and it is commented that iron must be shot; and we say that gumma is caused in the marriage, and great caution in its cure, and they tell the old man that when gums are in the body or can be removed if there are as many gums as chancres which are in the mammillae, and in the fissures, and in the like places, and it must be all done when it is at the beginning; and when it is large and old, if not able to approach it, for I have never seen a cured one; nor has anyone ever been cured before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide I boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	1. And the operation, when it is in the body or can be opened, is that you never purge the patient with black charcoal; then make it healthier if there is manifest fullness, then cut the bone in the leg to make the operation; then your shoulder bones or chin become green, and all the hair falls out, and the bone of all parts feels nothing left; leave the wound completely drained, and press well on the limb with your hand or on anything, and let the dislocation correct itself if it deviates from the incision of the artery or vein, as long as cauterization is not done; then another cure until it is healthy.
de ydropisie	The first sentence to translate is "de ydropisie
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer: lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	The first sentence to translate is "de ydropisie". In the division of symptoms, we have discussed the appearances of dropsy, and how the assembly of the pulse is made, and the signs of each appearance, and the cure done by medicines, and that which is cured by fire: if it is only; and should one touch iron in these two appearances: this means, tympanites and hydrops, since this is a mortal thing; therefore, when you medicate the dropsy appearance called "eclites" of medicines, and the cure does not profit, if you look at whether the maladies are weak, or if there is another disease than dropsy, if all and solution of the stomach and such things; if it does not touch iron, because it has doubt; and if you see that the patient is very green, and only has dropsy, and it is not too little nor too much, then you should over: gently hold the patient with your hands, and press the belly to the lowest part of the pit, then take the spatula according to this form.
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	And so, let us proceed to Section II.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier; puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu; puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	And so, let us proceed to Section II. If the point is not entering but only reaching the intestine when it is removed, and it cannot be cut, then look at whether the discharge is directed towards the intestines: if it is, then you must cut from the left side of the boude III; and if it is due to disease of the liver, then your cut should be on the right side of the boude III; and if it is due to mucus, then it should be on the left, and not just the mucus but also the excess that runs to the weak part of the belly; then perforate all the skin with the instrument, and the boute, and lighten your hand on all the surrounding area between the skin and the syfac as you would when scooping out a quantity of dough or soil; then perforate the syfac as soon as the surrounding area begins to come together at the left six, and that is the end of the abscess, then remove the instrument from this side, and if it is the form:
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus; et II d’autre part, et I d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	And it resembles a silver needle, and is light or feather-light, and in the part of the socket there is a small puncture; and sometimes it costs three punctures, and twice others, and once more, and it is the head cut so as to resemble a pen, and this is the shape of the incision that the scribes make with the pen.
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort; mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit; fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	At the head of the wound, if you see that when it bleeds, now take the instrument away; empty the first part or the third, for if you see more than there should be in that hour, by chance it may be the end of the man's life due to the resolution of his spirit towards the weapon, or he may die from weakness, or he may be near death; but according to the quantity of his virtue, and according to what the dispositions of his virtue signify, and his wounds; then take away the instrument and hold the wound, and it will be held now by the part that is swollen around the puncture which I have spoken of, so that you may see how to do it; then resume the instrument the next day, if you see the man suffering as he does, and take a small quantity of astringent; do this every day, and keep from bleeding as much as possible but only a little blood.
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	When you doubt the patient's condition and let them drink water, if the care for the grave or sand bath is needed, and by washing or bathing and in the sun, and it becomes flushed; and the care of drying medicines as soon as they are healthy, and cauterizing on the stomach and liver and spleen after the removal of the fever, as I have said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	of the stopping of the growth
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	No child is born without having had a fever, or if the fever is small, or it is not in their chest.
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	If the patient does not see anything at all, even the most subtle things according to this form:
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	Then place the catheter subtly and tie it with the string, and leave it for 3 to 4 days or more until the patient sees urine being made, if it is closed, let the urine pass and then replace it. And by chance, no one will close it, because the urine that comes out does not leave closed.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	If the catheter is small, if it is medicated with a plug of cloth as we have said, if it stretches.
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	Those who do not have the catheter in their groin are bleeced, because no one is born with a catheter at the tip of the vagina, for if they pee before it does not lose its vagina up; and they cannot enjoin because of this, because the material cannot come just to the marriage, and it is a very bad disease.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	1. And the manner of the cauterization is that if the patient gushes blood on his back, it is the head of the thorn and its tail is as large as a pen's point, if it pierces the flesh; and you must prevent the loss of blood that often occurs, and if it does, if the wound is infected, and treat the wound until it heals.
des pustules de la verge	1. of thorn's pustules
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a I oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	1. Many times, pus comes out of the thorn in the back, and it has an unpleasant appearance; and among them are malignant and non-malignant; if you prescribe them to the subcutaneous tissue, and cut and remove all of them, then put on cotton wool soaked in Egyptian ointment; then the treatment of the ointment is done as long as it is healthy.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	If the tumor is malignant, of a dark color and sizeable, then you must perform a fire cautery.
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	After removing the tumor, if it is still growing, and has both hairy and bald parts, then you must remove the remaining bald part; and if it continues to grow, then the cure for the bald part.
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	For if you remove the entire tumor at once, and do not leave any part of it, and it becomes black and corrupted in its place and outside; then all that is black and corrupted must be treated with honey and flour made from the scraps of grape vines and wheat, then the cure of other cures as long as it is healthy.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	And if blood comes out of the wound, then follow this form of the moon cautery:
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars; et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	And if blood comes out of the wound, then follow this form of the moon cautery: it is knowledge, at the discharge of sanguine and corruption; and if the head of the thorn is corrupted and retracts, then you must cut or lead a rope around the thorn and piss out the salve among; and when the hair arrives at the end of the thorn which has not been circumcised, or has come by wound or abscess, then it comes to pass that you scrape it with the instrument knife, as long as the roots are loose and free from the thorn; and if this is a difficult matter to do, then you must scrape it with the spatula of any part of the thorn and the hair; then pour some element between them, and put a subtle fold of wet linen on the cold edge, so it does not return.
de la circoncision	The first sentence to translate is: "Ou cautere
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not more difficult than other wounds; however, if we make this work of our own will, and properly as for our children, it is the best work and the most gentle for health.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not commonly circumcise their children, for they do not use it in their law, and have only what we have acquired by experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor I dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a II toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	For I want the greatest part of masters and doctors who made circumcision in the old way, and with force, and at all ages; if it were possible to kill them, for it has two threads, and by chance if one of them is cut, and the other remains, then that one is dead.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	Or they return, and the pain is double, and at circumcision which is done quickly, there is no assurance of the point of the member; and at the circumcision of the ring by chance it breaks the iron, and wounds the skin, and many times are born without any means of circumcision, and I want that.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	From the mondification that is made with forces on all the strand of the thread, I have found its benefit in the experiment, for the forces cut equally as well as from above and below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien; et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge; puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	For when you press your hand, if it cuts evenly all the way through; but that the thread be well twisted around the bow; and that the first stitch be of the right kind, as if the child could understand that you only tie the thread around the bow, and then tighten it in all the ways you can think of; then tie it straight between your hands, and put the forces between your hands or on your fingers which the child cannot see, and then blow your hand on the bow and lift it as high as the tip of the bow is assembled, then mend well the dung that is in it, then tie the leash with a double thread, then tie the other line; and hold it tightly between the second knot and the index finger, and twist the loop around the thumb and the index finger, then loosen the knot gently and take out the tip of the bow; then leave the sand pouch and pouch, for they are the most difficult; and put some powder on it and on the powdered glue made from a piece of cooked beef cut into small pieces, cured with olive oil, and fresh, and leave it suspended over another day, and the cure will continue as long as it is healthy.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The form of the forces at the wounding is this: the two heads are thin and sharp, and are as strong as the arm.
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	The error of wounding if it occurs when the edges come out of the incision; therefore, it is necessary to extend it to your nail, unless the edge becomes septic; and it should be done correctly, and if you do not hold it with your nail, then the wound.
Et s’il trespassent III jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	And if they pass three years, and the wound is infected, if you let it be as long as the septic matter is quieted, and gently burned, and if the wound is not infected, it will not harm you.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	1. Cure the limb with substances that have powdered plague, which we have mentioned or treated as powders, and if it does not work, then it will become worse; cure the limb as we have said, as long as it is healthy.
dou retenement de l’urine	2. Hold back the urine.
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division; et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e; et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	3. If the urine is bloody, or if there is gangrene of the wound, or of the bowels, or of the intestines, or of similar things, as we have said in the division; and if the urine is discharged, and you see that it is retained by the urethra, which is at the top or bottom of the bladder, then it is necessary to place the vessel on the back, and extend the abdomen from the part near the back, and restrict the male member as much as possible; and then it is necessary to constrict the bladder at the expression of the urethra, because if the urine is discharged, and it is not, if as we have said, and the male member feels great pain, then it is necessary to perform an extraction with all instruments that are called "siringue", of which the form is: and it should be a thin silver hair, like the tail of an owl; and it should be the tooth of a palm tree half an inch long, and it should be thin at the root.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede; puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine; et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	1. And the manner of the urine's exit if you take a double thread and tie it around the waist of linen or cotton, and cut the waist of the thread at the umbilicus; and cut off the excess of the linen and cut the umbilicus, then anoint the umbilicus with oil or broom and ointment of urine and urine of ox, and make the patient sit on the seat, and the patient empties the bladder and the verge with moist oil and olive oil and French thyme; then gently place the thread in the verge as it reaches the root of the verge, then double the verge towards the bowel; then cut the thread before the bladder, and feel the patient come before the empty bladder, and this is done according to this order because either the patient or the bowel will be turned; then the thread goes through all the linen pouches and the urine follows the linen, then it is withdrawn further, and the urine is made up; and the siringue resumes when the bladder is empty and the bowel is healed.
des maladies de la vessie	Of diseases of the bladder
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When there is scorching or burning in the bladder, or when an abscess forms, and you see water and medicines distilling, then do this to all the instrument called "clyster," and it is shaped like:

Caution: In the section of this ramie, there are many difficulties, so I think it is better to leave it; I will now describe the ovary and the appearances of the abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	I say therefore that all abscesses come from wounds, and also from nails; it is by chance.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion; et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief; et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	It is to know that the abscess is caused by superfluous sweet and acrid matter, which is spread on the nails, or by percussion; and the color of the abscess is according to the color of the wound; and it does not cause pain, and it is an abscess of grief, and sometimes it is grayish-blue and purple, and of fuscous color, and never comes from an artery or a vein.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois; et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	When it is of an artery, if it is located by the arrangement of the abscess, when you press on it with your two hands; and only then will you be able to touch it.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars; et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	That which is made of gut is located by the arrangement of the vein, and can be well made in this shape and in others, and it is that you cut off the crotch, then the wound is at the top, and the blood is white and clear, and deliver the suspensory from all parts of the wound.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope; et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	If the urethra is already stopped with these wounds, then it must be that you draw the urethra and cut; and if it is full of serum, or in this case where the veins are obstructed, then it must be that you deliver all of this, and the cut recoils.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	If the birth of the child is from the lower part of the body, and you manage to catch it all, and remove the head, as we have said.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If your wounds are completed, then use the smooth woolen plaster in oil and rosewater, and then continue with other treatments as needed to become healthy.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the boils
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait; et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	This is a remedy for boils enveloped in a wrap similar to a bandage, with the softening of the boils, and the patient should be still quiet when it happens; the treatment of this disease is well done as far as we know, and all we can tell you about the wound, according to what was done in the past.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment; puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples; puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief; puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues; puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions; car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz; si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	1. It is necessary that you shave the patient's leg below the knee, then cut the bandage according to your two hands, all the threads that are close to the edge, and tie the knots; then apply a sponge large enough to cover all the veins, as much as possible, and then scrape over each part, as we have said in the extraction of arteries in the temples; then take a needle or if it has a double thread, tie it at the first place where the blood came out, and tie it to the other end; then cut it according to the length of the wound, following the longest course, and in the veins that are corrupted; then cure the wound as we do with other wounds, if no vein is bleeding, and if all the veins come out, then tie the knots at all the veins; if the patient loses his grip due to the incision of the veins, and the threads are cut and cannot be helped.
de la routure dou syfac	From the rupture of the facial bone
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions; et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses; et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement; et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	When the rupture of the facial bone occurs, it is either by section or extension, or the intestines descend to one of the groins; and this fracture is either due to facial trauma or extension, and these methods of injury come from various causes: either percussion, jumping, biting, or tightening the grief face, and in similar ways; and the signs when it is an extension of the facial bone are that there is little and little, in long tension, and does not suddenly come; and it is the abscess equal to the parfent until the front, because the facial trauma presses on the intestines.

And the sign is when it is of the section of the small intestine, which brings on sudden pain at the beginning, and it appears in different places, not near the skin, and this is from the intestine and the heart due to the inflammation of the small intestine.

aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait IIII filz; puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de II pars; And the treatment of iron for pain, if it cannot be avoided, is as follows: If the intestine is cut, and it can be held in check, and causes great pain to the patient, even when pressed; then open the wound with your hand, and cleanse it with warm water; then sew the edges of the wound with threads according to what you have used to open the wound, so that the suture does not come out; then scarify the inflamed part of the small intestine, as far as the white clay is visible on both sides; then close the wound with your left hand, and hold the blanc syfac above your right hand; and stretch the uterus towards the tail; and command the midwife to extend the uterus, and remove any intestine or white clay that is entangled behind it; then take a needle or a thick thread made of four filaments, and sew it in the rear part of the inflamed part, which is after the small intestine; then assemble the threads one on top of the other in a cross shape, and around the blanc syfac, as we have said, which is behind the small intestine, with a strong thread of two parts; then enclose the threads of the clyster, and form them into a knot of two parts, so that no vessels that are cut can enter the uterus, and the string does not break; and leave the first knot according to the second knot, and after these two knots let the blanc syfac which is behind the small intestine be as wide as the uterus carries it; then close the wound with the remaining threads, and sew them in the part that is behind the small intestine, as far as the white clay does not stick to the string, and the bow, as we have said before; then apply olive oil, and put on plaices, and sew the string that we have mentioned.

des emorroides	The text translates to: "Due to the dislocation
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	Emorroydes are wounds that without proper care become infected, and when they become infected, they become thelul; and we have said in the division of appearances and signs, and I will say those that receive treatment.
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I say that wounds and infected wounds, when they are made in the flesh, do not appear until treatment is given by fire.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those that are in the mouth of the patient can be felt, and they can be treated.

Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	And if it is inflamed, it is bad.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu. And when the abscess is closed, if the wound is cured as soon as it is healthy; and the one called "albathir" is red and resembles the sharp point of a knife, as I have said before; and then the wound is cured as soon as it is healthy.
des apostemes de la marris	Of abscesses of the arm

Throughout, the corners should be more subtle and restrictive, and made of flat or round wood; and the mouth should be no wider than a thumb, and the margins of the branches should be long and narrow, and at least half a palm and a quarter of a palm; and these two jaws should be firmly held in place, with one end fixed and the other free, or a quarter of a palm more; and these two jaws are inserted into the mouth of the shoulder to open when turning the corners.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles; et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large; et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes; puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	1. Another form, in its appearance more subtle and lighter, is made of flat or square wood, according to the appearance of the nails; and it has two edges, as you see, like a palm of the hand, and they are wide; and when you open the mare, as you see with all the instruments, if you place the woman on the bed, the thighs and legs spread out, then adjust the two edges and the nails in the mare, and hold the instrument's handle firmly between your fingers; then operate all the instruments, as you have done with the nails evenly, according to the quantity you see open the mare's mouth, until the bride faces what she sees.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	1. This instrument is all around, and its appearances are multiplied; when one sees them, the more they work, the higher they rise in quantity.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	2. If you do not despise the instrument that you have not seen, because its needs are not easily overcome.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis; et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	3. When the second child is born, if you command the midwife to hold the placenta, and then carefully remove it from the body, and force your hands to the mouth and nose; and if it jumps because of this, so be it.
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire; toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	4. If the child does not jump, and if I can, and perform an episiotomy or perineotomy, and place herbs that may open the mother's mouth, such as calamus, rue, anise, chamomile, and cassia, all of which are cooked or pounded with water on fire; then place a cork or plug in the mother's mouth, and the other end in her mouth, and tighten it as much as the vapor leaves the mother's mouth; then remove it, as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If the second leap fails.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction; mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	And if she remains after this treatment, and it does not improve, then command the patient to take their left hand in oil of sesamum or musk, and then apply it to the wound, and then remove it; when she finds it, she should gently stretch it out a little on both sides, so that the wound does not slip during extraction. But she must then move lightly to the right and left, and then draw it out. If she comes and it heals.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes; et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire; mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon; si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	And if the mouth of the wound is too tight, we have called for the treatment of stretching and fumigation with herbs; and if it does not do all that we have said, then keep from pulling on it; but it is likely that what is in the mouth of the wound, you will tie it to the woman's thigh, then apply ointment of tetrafarmaçon; if it pierces and returns, and comes out stronger, but all the same, if it pierces so much that it has a bad smell in the stomach and head, and makes the patient sick.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	If it comes that there are successful fumigations in this way: no of the ancients have tried fumigation of cresson and dry figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The form of the instrument is such that it fumigates the woman with the retention of flowers and the secondine if this is:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu; et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	And it seems like a dog, and one puts the subtle head in nature, and the wide shoulders under the fire; and it is the fumigations with charcoal, and the ash as much as it is gray, and another one begins again.
de percier lou fondement	to see if the foundation is good.
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many children are born who do not perceive the foundation well, but if they have some subtle face: if it comes to the task of perceiving that face in its own way, and not perceiving anything from spatulum agut, and grasp the handling that it does not touch; then put on a fine powder in wine and oil, and the cure of ointment as much as it is healthy.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	If you doubt that it will not stay in place, if you put or puncture a needle into it, and let it go, and be careful when the child sees it going to bed.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And never comes this help without great pain or hemorrhage; if it happens, if you can mend it: if we have said about the needle in the skin.
de la fistule dou fondement	of the fistula formed.
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	Fistulas that come from the side of the wound are nodular, and grow, if they come from the edges of the wound, or in the space between them; and when this nodularity is old, it becomes hard and swells, and sometimes becomes blue or purple, and never are these fistulas permanent; they are known by the fact that they are due to vomiting or diarrhea when the patient vomits, and sometimes happen by chance.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	If there are fistulas that pierce the uterus and a large part of the vagina; and they reach the joint of the coccyx and the neck of the anus.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	If you cannot find the fistula at its base, and it is not tortuous: then use your index finger or a thin needle to enter the fistula as far as possible, until you reach the anus.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit; et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit: saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	If there is tortuosity, then use a small tent or horsehair to enter the fistula as far as possible, until you feel the tent or hair with your finger; and if you do not feel it, and there is no emesis, no straining, or no discharge, then follow what we have said: cut it if it does not pass; if you need to cure it quickly.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	When the fistula is present in the bladder or led from the urethra, if it leaks and cannot be stopped by medicines.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu; s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement; et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	If it is perceived at the junction of the thigh, if it leads to the knee; if it has tortuosity and excessive pain, if it causes constipation and no medicine can stop it; and in these fistulas there is no cure other than labor and vanity of the lazy who enter into them.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	In the one that is not a true fistula and not an ancient one, with hope for health through iron, as I have experienced, and it is that the patient's hand is on his back; and he leans his legs until they are against his thighs, and his thighs are inclined to his belly; then make a tent of blankets, or of plunk if it has tortuosity, as long as you are careful or the test comes.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	When the patient feels pain at the base, if it is detected that you have reached the end of your index finger, it feels as if it is trying to perceive; and if you discover or feel between your thumb and index finger, the nail or the claw, then you should check if it is intact; if it cannot be mended and cannot be healed.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	It is difficult to heal all wounds, but this is not the case; and if you can, then do this: if the cautery is made according to the size of the fistula as mentioned earlier, then insert the bougie completely into the fistula until it reaches the base; and leave it there for 2 or 3 days, until you feel that these charred parts are hard, which resemble a quill like an ostrich feather; then the dressing of softened char and soaked char.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If it is in good health, then it is well.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	If it is not in good health, then it cannot be healthy; and if it tries to enter, and does not pierce the skin at the bottom where it should be, and between your thumb and index finger put a thick covering of char or smoke, and you will see the fistula at this point that shows the covering through; if the cope starts at the beginning of the fistula, and ends before the tent, and then cauterize after, as it goes to the end of the tent; and it will be released from the tent, and will hurt; then the charred parts that seem like a needle of a swallow will be broken, and none will remain.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	If it does not harm you, and cuts between you and the wound, whether by fire cauterization or medicinal heat.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	For fire cauterization has two effects: it knows the surgery of these joints, and the stopping of blood and the relief of swelling; then the care of wounds softened in the belly or in the thigh, as long as they do not hurt, and it is left in place; then care for the wound of sour sores enchaned with dry char, and these are the dry medicines.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, if it is healthy and does not return often.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if a fistula comes suddenly with great force, and it is moved away from the body, if the vessel is damaged or not, and inquire about it.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	If you feel the tendon, and enter II is the fabric or the scar, or it is close to perforating, if not it was only a sign of marriage and hope, by the administration of one of the three ways: or you cauterize as we have said, or you cope justly in front, or if you see that it has many tents and cures as desired; and do not move too much in front, that you do not cut the tendon that holds the foundation, and vie for the excretions through the desired sense; then the cure, as we have said; by chance if it is healthy, or you remove that covering and the mundue then when it is coped with the fundament, or by tent or another instrument appointed; then mend the char made in the wound as much as you can; then study to restore the wound, and to delay the fistula in the part behind the foundation: if it is still a lighter thing for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	And no time have fistulas been made in this manner: and when you reach the end of the fistula, it is either flat or has a doughy consistency like the skin above it, if you take a tent according to this form:
Et i boute I fil tort en II, et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And if you cut it in two, and cut the tent all along the fistula as far as it reaches the head:
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	If it is perpendicular to the doughy part of the skin, cut the thread along the fistula as far as it reaches the head; then remove the tail of the thread, and assemble the two ends, and stretch them apart, and leave one or two; and keep them together until the threads meet again, and curl around each other; then treat the wound as much as it is sore and healing.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not perforate, if you try to open it in all possible ways that you can think of, it will not be too difficult.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it is not advisable to make a cut through the lacing if it is possible, and then the treatment, as we have said, until it is healthy.
