des emorroydes	of embalmed bodies.
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	1. Dislocations are classified into two ways: either they are due to the foundation, like resin grains, and they have small and large ones, and some are cut off, and they have one or more, and they weaken the foundation and the head of the foundation; but those that are weakened have little moisture, and they are cut off or a small piece of turquoise or a small piece of sinew, and they have the color of the core; and the treatment of those who have weakened the foundation is that you order the patient to spit out in chambers as much as the foundations become, and when the foundations are firm, and the offspring appear; if you hurry, and you can catch them with tweezers, or you hold them in your nails, then you cut them at their roots; and if they cannot be held by their moisture, then they are laid flat, or on a cloth, or a piece of linen; and they are taken out of your two hands, then they are cut, and you powder some hot powders that are in the cauterization lewer; or you cauterize them as it is said in the cauterization chapter, so that other cures can cure them as long as they are healthy; and if they cannot issue, then they are clisterized with clister mouth and sharp teeth, and you wash what is under the foundation, so that it can issue openly; and if the patient's mouth is not preened, and the filaments are weak in the foundation, then it is the lightest cure; and if you preen them with your nails or tweezers, and they are cut off, then they are cured as we have said, so that they are healthy and do not fear the incision by fire.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it comes to your attention that you need to adjust the stitching according to this method: take one thread, thread it through an awl, and then pull the thread on the other side, and turn the two ends of the other thread around the awl, and if it is too wide; and then tighten the thread, then knot the thread, and draw out the awl, and do the same for the rest, and leave the excess suture at the top of the suture; then put the foundation fabric on the wavy edge with oil rosette or cerulean, and put the foundation, and command the patient to lie down; and then leave it as long as it does not change, and when it will change, if the cure for ointment and other cures, then it is healthy.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	The first sentence to translate is "dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement". The translation of this line is
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	For many times there have been sediments in the intestines, and by constriction of nature, and when the disease is old and medicine does not help.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it comes to passing a spatula or your nail at the spot of an abscess or the scar of the wound, which does not allow moisture; then treat it as much as possible, and if it does not heal, then repeat the incision as soon as it is safe, and soak it in hot water and dry it; then treat it as much as possible.
dou fremit	The first line of the text translates
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	Antonin is a small insect that should be present in the chest, and it moves around; and never does the patient feel it, and it is felt to be like death's tremor, and it comes throughout the chest, and more in the hands than in any other part.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	If the cure is that you take a thorn from a sheep's hoof, or a vulture's beak, and place it on the tremor, as long as the purple circle encircles the tremor entirely; then turn your hand over all the thorn until you cover all around the tremor, and place it in front, and draw out the tremor from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see, if I make this of a bone or iron in this form, and it is subtle and thin and through:
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	If you do not see, if it does not move, and if it is in front or in the chapter of cauterization:
de la forme dou clistere	of the form of the cyste:
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	Never has it been made of silver or archaut, or melted iron; and never has it been made of these small and large gashes, according to those that are used:
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Therefore, they are made in the care of children and the weak and painful, are small:
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The form of the small, large clister is such that it is placed wide, or the belly is made according to this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	And if it has a depression or the belly is depressed, as you see, and the head is perceived; and it is at one of the costals, and at the other; and the belly or places the medicines in a vessel of a beast or parchment, and perceives all the holes from small pertus, and between each pertus there must be a spice, then through each pertus thread the strong thread is passed, then assemble the belly as if it were a goat; and when the medicine is given, if the loop has the instrument before a strong thread, then clisterize; and this is the form of a circle:
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	1. And let the medicine not be too hot or too cold, and anoint the head with oil or unguent of urine or something similar, then lightly apply the ointment; then the surgeon takes his two hands and assembles them as much as possible, until it is all done, then he removes the bandage, and gently raises the patient's legs to the side, and if the medicine comes out, as much as it can; and if the patient sleeps a whole night, it will be more helpful.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	1. And if you dislocate the hip due to disease of the abdomen, and the medicine comes out, if it recurs as soon as it is healthy.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And if the swelling is or the abscess, or the phlegm, even if it is as subtle as that of a child; and this is the form of the subtle abscess when the skin is stretched.
des plaies	wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have said in the division of wound treatment; and you will say the treatments for hands and medicine, according to their completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to what they are made, and according to the parts where they are made, and how they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	The things made by wounds are made of the point of the piercing, and the size of the lancet or the lance, or the needle, or the spear, or other things; or according to the parts of the body, as a wound that is made at the neck, or at the shoulder, or the chest, or the stomach, or the liver, and similar members; and I will tell you the treatment for each wound, and I will mention simple wounds on the shoulder, as the memory will come to your chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	I say that when a simple wound comes or head, and the bone is not broken, if it is from cutting or similar things, and the skull is completely torn and the large wound is, you doubt slightly of hemorrhage: if it becomes safer of the head itself, if it comes little blood of the wound, and it is healthier on the opposite part of the belly; and avoid the excess of wine and large meats.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it does not become safer, if the meat is anemic, and does not drink wine, and does not eat fat; and puts on the wound, if it clots comes, thin oil or olive oil only, or in vinegar steeped; and if it does not clot, if it puts on the wound, it is fresh at all its sanc, and it is not moved by the air, dust, which I will say a little later; and if it has been moved, if it puts on some ointments, as long as it is healthy.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large like that of a spearhead and its appearance, and the lips cannot be reassembled by tents, if they can be assembled by stitching, just like I will say for belly wounds, by sewing.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	If the wound is discovered to be of bone, it may be, and only holds by a point, if the cloth; then cure the wound with medicine, and restore hardness in the leather of the thigh, and instruct the patient to eat large meats, such as testes and cooked flour, as well as poultry, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if you cut or scarify the flesh, and it does not reach the bone, if the wound is large, then cure it; and if arteries have been cut in the wound or vein, which cannot be stopped by medicines, if one wants to stop it, and you delay the wound, if the edge of a thread; and if it does not benefit, if the cauterized.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	If these wounds are small and simple, then the cure is light: and it is that you apply this powder which is always dry when the doctor has touched it.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And the way of the powder is: take a part of incense; saffron two parts; live chalz three parts, and the fine powder, and apply it to the wound, and pull it tight, until it sticks well and adheres to all its sanc; then the powder is well, and it is left to drip if it does not enfle, for one does not want to use the medicine more than it is healthy.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And never once made is it done solely with heat, when there is no candle or blood of the dragon, but that the wound has been touched by the art.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the art has touched the wound, immediately in this way; but use some digested ointments, or dough made from flour of barley and honey, until it blooms; then apply other cures as necessary until it is healthy.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	And if the bone fracture comes with the wound, and it is small, if it is extracted with fine tweezers; and I will tell you more about this later in the chapter.
de la plaie dou col	From the wound of the knee
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If the wound is simple, it does not differ from the other knee, but if it is a deep knee wound or the artery is compressed.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	If it is a deep knee wound, if there is no other choice but to leave the treatment, and nothing else should restrict it, because it will heal and pull back; and do not put anything on the wound, because the substance of the nerves is cold, and its continuation is with the brain, which is the more delicate member; but if medicine is available, like cool water rinsed with oil rose, and the wound washed in the same way with cool water, and other piercings according to this method, and moistened bandages.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, and it is bound with bandages, then the cure will be done once it is healthy.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	And if the wounds are deep and full of bones, and it is pricked or lower down the leg; and if the artery is cut, and blood flows from the wound, and the cauterization is done as best as possible; and if the spine of the neck or the throat is pricked, or the jaw, and it is held, by which the meat goes, if the bone is cut at the corner of the neck, and it is replaced according to its natural figure; then the extraction is done, and a few jaws are left, and the care of discharges is done as much as possible when it is healthy; and if the wound has made an impression on the bone, if you want; and if there are pieces of bones, if they are taken out as soon as possible, and those that you do not want to take out, if you leave them as much as the wound is bleeding, and it is healed and allied to the issue; and if the wound is fresh, and powder is put on as I have said.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	If there is an abscess in the wound and it has formed a fistula, as I have described in my chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	from the wound of the arrow or the spear
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	If it is a wound from an arrow or spear, and the wound is deep, then look at the wound's vitality: if it is mortal, then the wound is dead; but if it is not deep, and it is fresh all around its base, then do not put anything in the first hour, but give it powder and keep the wound clean, and revive the patient; but if you have ointment, then put a piece of cotton in the wound for suction to remove moisture, and make the patient sleep on the wound for three or four hours, or more, until the spasms, trembling, and contractions of the chest are gone; and when you see the bones in good order, then know that the wound is saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	1. Cure the wounds with suitable remedies and other treatments as much as possible; and if it cannot be cured, apply poultices made from herbs that have been boiled, and continue the treatment until it heals.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	1. If the wound is cut with a razor or scalpel, and it is simple, either on the surface or on the back, if the care of the one who is in front; if it is large, it is sanded; if it is small, it is powdered, and if it penetrates into the bone and into pieces, if the wound allows, and if they are removed when they come out; if they do not come out, let it be left exposed to air, if it is trimmed; and for other wounds, the judgments of other parts are as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	2. With great difficulty of the stomach
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	1. The abdominal dislocations are large and many, and there is no intestinal rupture once or twice; the sutures are more painful, and no small wound can compare to the large ones, so the intestines are reinserted more times, unless they are reinserted in pieces; because the intestines swell so much that they feel pain, if they return more times, and because the other wounds are more painful, because the abdominal sutures are more common than those of other parts, and the other sutures are also common in other wounds; all of them are more painful with the abdominal suture, and I will say one by one and declare each.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	I say that when the wound is small, and there is no damage to the intestines, and it is easy to set, this is one of the two ways: either by the size of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestine is twisted due to the blow.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And when it is twisted, handle it in this way: soften a sponge or a piece of cloth only, or you can use hot water and cut and scrape, and gently pull the intestine as much as it is twisted; and never do this without causing damage, and it will become untwisted.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	When you see the flame departing, if the intestine is hot or cold and swollen, it is because the entrance of a little thing is causing this; and if it cannot enter, then make a small wound with the instrument and cut through the tissues; and the first cure is to cut off the part that does not need to be cut, without causing great harm, and this is the cause for fever: if it cuts through the tendons but does not heal, and then it forms.
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	When the wound is enlarged and the intestine jumps out, if you put it back in accordance with its natural form in its own place, if you can, because this is beneficial.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	When the wound is wide, and it is in the lower abdomen, if you can make the patient lie on his back and raise his legs higher than his chest; and if it is in the lower abdomen, then he should raise his chest and thighs higher than the surrounding areas, and thus the wound in the one side will be higher than the other; and you must manage this in large and dirty wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	When the wound is small, and it is in the lower abdomen, if you can make the patient lie on his back and raise his legs higher than his chest; and if it is in the lower abdomen, then he should raise his chest and thighs higher than the surrounding areas, and thus the wound in the one side will be higher than the other; and you must manage this in large and dirty wounds.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I opened the intestine and it had been there for 24 hours, and it was a wound that was 15 years old, and I treated it, and it became healthy.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And the mirror showed that it would die, and this was a miracle; and I did not treat it with any medicine, because there was none in our league, nor any medicines; and I washed more than twice a day on the wound, and the gauze of honey as soon as it became healthy.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	Or you will tell me the two proper ways of stitching: take the needle, and thread it through the edge of the wound; when it has perceived the right direction in the right place, if you have the end of the suture or thread that you have threaded the needle with, and make it perceive from another part of the denuded part; and the stitches are understood if you do as the barber does the hair, and leave once the wax on one side, and take it back again on the other, until the stitching is complete.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	The second method of sewing, which Galen calls his own, is the one that most people use, where they naturally bring together the two ends and apply one of the needles to the other, in this way: take an awl or a needle point close by, and pierce it into the material; then leave the two needles; then turn the awl, and pierce it into the part that is closest to the edge of the material, as the needles are; then pierce the other part of the edge of the material with the other needles that are on the opposite side; and this is the most common way of sewing.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	When the patient hears this advice and no one else confirms it, we must cut the belly with the feathers, or as many as necessary; and we must insert one feather on one side and the other on the other, in the manner of those who are twisting; and if the rupture is near the belly, then the wound is more painful than others in the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	The judgment of the wound is if it is like the judgment of other wounds: and if you touch the fresh wound with all its blood, then if it has not moved, it must reinsert the intestine and close the hole; then put some powdered charcoal on it, and if it has not moved, then put any ointment that is present, as long as the wound is bowed; and cut the fillet, and be sure of the suture, and the mirror; then treat the wound as you would with other wounds, until it is sound; and if you have no medicines, then put them, as much as they come out to grip the belly, a cloth full of vinegar, and shake it twice the morning until it is sound.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	For you do not have other knowledge in other conditions than wounds are simple; and if you doubt that the wound does not cause commonality to the members, then it comes that you lighten slightly in oil of temperate chalor, or oil rose, and put on the gauze, and dress the wound; and if there is pain or fever in the belly, and many times come, if the clysterize with red wine, and at the same time the fever comes to the intestine; and the percute, and soothe that when it is the large intestines, it is lighter to heal than the small.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The small intestine, also known as the "young" intestine, cannot heal while it is inflamed, and this is due to the sensitiveness of its walls and the closeness of its nature to the nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	If the gallstone jumps out of the wound, and it is reset as quickly as possible while it is fresh; and if it becomes black and turns gray, then you must note the black leu that was there, because it has lost its blood and arteries; then treat what is between the ligaments, and pull the heads away from the part of the wound up to where the gallstone is coming out, and the wound is bowed.
de la routure dou boueil	Of the rupture of the bowels
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	When the intestine is ruptured and the wound is small, if it can be restored with a few stitches, because I have seen that some were healed or stomach wounds from a lance; and it was the wound on the left side of the stomach, and became an abscess and fistula, and in it was the ejection and vomiting; I treated according to what I could, and did not stop subtleting until it was healed, and I called it.

And when I saw it was sutured, I doubted that the patient had no harm in his belly; but he had none, but he delayed in better conditions, and drank and ate; and they said to any experimenters that when a small wound is in the intestine, one must stitch it in this way: first stretch the testicles as much as possible, then assemble the lips of the wound, and when the mouth has overstretched the lips, put it between the lips if it can be held; then close the testicle, and it will stay if it cannot slip, then make another stretch in the same way that before, as long as the wound is completely covered; and sew the wound.

de fistule ou qu’ele soit	Of a fistula or if it is
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	It is said that all wounds and abscesses, when they heal, if they are called universally "fistula", and at the same time if they are smooth and round.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	And a fistula is according to the belief of nodulation, which is hard and full of pus, and one feels pain, and is as smooth as the tail of an owl; and never in a clear jump, and sometimes thick; never small, and sometimes large; never shallow, and sometimes deep; and I have seen this in the division of wounds, that all wounds which are not healed, and there is no pain, it is only due to one of the seven causes: it is to know, by a little pain or corrosive substance; or by malice; or because the pus is too hard, and comes out through the lips, which does not leave any pain; or there are too many bowels; or the lesion is porous, and the matter is of bad quality; or the medicine is not good in the cure; or because the corruption is like a pestilence; or because the property in the region is delayed digestion, and delayed health, and runs by nature; or there are ulcers or bones: and I have shown all these causes and their signs and remedies with medicines in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	The text translates to: "And it is necessary for me to inform you of the treatment for fistulas, which is made by human hands.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus. The text translates to: "Fistulas can occur in all parts of the body; for there are fistulas that come from large veins, arteries, nerves, or the face, or intestines, or the bladder, or any of the costal bones, or the spine, or any joint of the hands or feet; and if it comes to affect the principal member, it is similar to these. dou feu	The first sentence to translate is "Ou

de l’aposteme de l’ungle	Of the abscess of the finger
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	Gangrene is an abscess that arises from the finger, either the thumb or the other, or by chance in other parts; and when it becomes infected, if it is not cared for, then the abscess suppurates and rot and putrefy as it reaches the root of the finger, and in rare cases it reaches the entire finger; and it comes to the corrosions of the bone, as there is pain, and it is the head that becomes large, and the color turns foul.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	When you treat it as we have said in the division, and the cure does not profit, then you must cut off all the excess that is grown on the finger, then cauterize the wound after.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	1. The fire cautery is a great help when the bone is healthy, and the nail is healthy; and if the nail presses on the skin, and it begins to prick, and burn, then you should cut off the nail that points the skin, and draw it up, and apply some subtle and gentle medicine under the skin, and then treat the wounds as they heal.

des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	Of the verses that are born between leather and char
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	This disease is called in our land "disease of beef" because it often occurs in the shoulder, and is a small worm that passes between leather and char, and goes up and down throughout the body, and sends pain to every limb as it goes through the skin or flesh; and it is caused by certain humors, such as serpents, snakes, and worms, and ascarios or intestines; and one doubts its evil, because when it passes through the body, it goes to the head, and comes to the oil, by chance enters, and destroys the oil; and this happens many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	When you see the patient being cured and dressing, if it cannot be otherwise, then if you find that the limb is tightly bound with a strong bandage, then cut it and take it off, and put it in the char, and do not tie it, if the cauterization by fire is done as mentioned, until it is dead; and the greatest harm it can cause, if it comes to the oil, as we have said; and if you see it coming near the oil, if the hair is tightly tied around it, then cut it off, and take it off; and it is necessary to use the cautery of mundification of liquid medicines for the humors of the patients, and avoid foods that are spicy for nourishment.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	From the pain that comes from dislocation
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	This disease is known in our country as "wakirig," and is a pain that comes in various parts of the body, and moves from part to part; and I see what I have told you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	I was called a female patient, and I saw my arm, and saw a small flesh in the vein of my wrist; and after a short time, I saw it rise as if it were a wire from the shoulder, more quickly than anything, as if it were gold when it is cut from the hand to another; the pain left that part, and moved to the shoulder, and then in a short time spread throughout the body, until it came to the other wrist; then she told me that she dislocated her shoulder, just as you see.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I was amazed to see how it moved from limb to limb, as I had never wanted this disease to happen in this way.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	Indeed, I wanted to make sure that the pain was not moving from one part of the body to another, but I did not want it to be so, as I see it in the woman; and I thought it was because the woman had hard breasts, and the veins were exposed, and because the constraint appeared due to this; and I did not know that according to this reason, it is not for those who are delicate and have moist breasts and veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	When you see this disease curing, and the patient feels that pain, if it opens as we have said, if the limbs and bones are weak, and then it is constrained to the bed; and cauterize the limb; and if you do not see with your eyes, the cure of this which relieves the weakness, if like pills of sassafras, and pills of snake root, and similar things.
des saiettes	arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are various, according to their appearances and according to the hardness of the horses' necks or not.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	The diversity of them is that some have large points, and small, and bristles, and scales; and some have angles, and some have tails, and some have pieces; and one that pierces in any member in different ways: or in the principal member, if it is like a chevelure, heart, liver, lung, spleen, intestine, uterus, vessel, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	When she finally reaches any joint of these limbs, and the sign of death appears that I will tell you later, it becomes apparent to you: if you want to avoid the extraction of this arrow, because death follows in its wake; and when this sign does not appear to you, and the wound is not deep, if it is not too late, and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And the sign of death appears when the arrow pierces the bone and comes out through the skin, and the part where the arrow entered is where the eye was, and it causes blackness and madness and fainting and pain in the limbs, and inflammation and pain in the tongue, and spasm and confusion of understanding, and vomiting of cold; and by chance it does not cause the nose or ears; and by chance it affects the speech and voice; and a jump of the white, moist wound seems like chills, and as a horse neighs; and if this sign appears to you, if you hold on to the treatment, and pull out the arrow if it is not deep.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	The sign of the shoulder when it pains or swells is that it is near the medial malleolus, and it feels as if it is becoming hard like a stone, not empty; and by chance the shoulder becomes as firm as the thigh, and in dark red blood comes out, and there is cold and cold frost, and sinking: then the signs of death begin to appear.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of the eye that is not moving is that there are no plains of ecchymosis from the wound, and the throat swells, and the face turns pale, and he gasps high and cries out in pain.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	1. If the arrowhead is in the covering of the breast, then it hits the small ribs; and it causes great pain and suffocation; and all the members of the shoulder move.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	2. If the arrowhead hits the stomach by chance, and there is no wound, then nothing digested in the meat.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	3. If the arrowhead hits the stomach and there is no wound, and there is no hope for the cure or the extraction of the arrowhead.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	4. If the arrowhead hits the bladder and the urine jumps out and comes out in a stream, and the patient feels great pain: fatal wounds.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other member, if the face and chest and shoulder and spine and the helper and the spinal column of the back and the forceps and the thighs, and the seeming member, are safe according to other dispositions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the artery is in the joint or the wound, and it is not visible, as I will tell you if I remember, because you are making the joint.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	I have seen a bone cut in the root of the nose: I tried to remove it, and it was stuck by the grease of the ear, but it was finally removed without much pain.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And then there was a case of an arrow that fell into the grease of the oil of ointment and stuck, and it was not possible to reach any further than the tip towards the other side, and it was as large as a Turkish bow, with no weight on the shoulders; the patient was healthy, and none of them had any accidents.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	And there was an arrow in the throat of a man, and it was the Arabian sauce for ears: I was the beards, and very subtle as I found it, and it was healthy for the men.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	And then there was an arrow in a man's chest or belly, and I thought he would die; and then after 30 days, if it did not change its position, I cut off the arrow, engaged it, and reset it, and it did not have any accidents.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	If you see a home where a boil or abscess is present, and it has been sutured; and the boil does not come out, and does not follow its natural dispositions, and does not find any harm in any of its natural works.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	If you see another man, where a boil is present in his face, and it has been sutured; and he does not suffer great pain; and there are other similar cases.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	If a boil is found in the face of a king, who was infected and declined on the left side; and the boil was fully healed three years later. I was called to care for it after it was healed.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	If you find the wound to be very tight.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	I tried it with all my subtlety and did not feel it; but I felt a sharp and painful prick in my left ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	I thought it was the tip of the arrow I had placed in the pus-filled abscess, because the wound did not swell; but I saw that it was actually from the arrow.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	I placed the plaster on my hand and squeezed the wound on the left side, and it took a long time for the pain to subside, until I felt the arrow in my shoulder; and he told me.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	I placed my hand on the poisonous wound that was infected, and felt the head of the arrow that had pierced the skin; then I continued to treat the wound with the poisonous medicine as soon as the head of the arrow became visible; it healed completely in four months, and then I excised the remaining parts of the arrow and my own nails, which I could not remove; therefore, I did not stop refining and inventing ways to extirpate it, as soon as I took hold of the wound with well-made needles, according to its form at the end of this chapter, as soon as I saw it, and restored the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	And the patient believes that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored: I will restore it therefore, and the wound was soothed and the patient was cured completely.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	I am telling you about the quality of extracting some arrows, if you put your care in what I say, because the books cannot make everything look beautiful; but the masters make the best use of a few good things, and of what is present and lacking, they do nine works, and nine instruments, from the descending of the things drawn down this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	I say that arrows do not come from the limbs or they are stuck in order according to two ways: either by the leg or they enter, or by another part; and the one that is thrown through the thigh or it enters, is an arrow that has entered into the flesh, and it has never been thrown once.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	If she does not jump now, if she lets the char stay until the hair is completely burned off and the end is clean; and then she gets stuck in the bone, and she cannot get out if there are no gaps, and each gap; and therefore she jumps, and if she jumps, if she perceives at any point that something is subtle inside, as long as the end is whitened, and then it slides out.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	And if the arrowhead gets stuck in the bone of the shoulder, and it wounds one of the major muscles, or any of the accidents I have mentioned to the barber: if he does not remove it at once, but leaves it until it is calmed after some time, for if he does not remove it, it will cause death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	When the bone is not broken only in the bone itself, and does not come out of place, and no other injury occurs, then the patient will recover without any problems.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is broken in two parts and cannot be put back in place, then if you manage to apply bandages immediately as I have told you, then treat the limb until it is healthy.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And if the bone is not visible in the limb, and you cannot see it, and you want to try everything; and if you feel it, if it does not fit any instrument; and if you do not want to cause further pain and swelling of the wound, and for the sake of the bone, and the cartilage, and there is no nerve or vein, then treat the bone as much as the wound is large; and then cut or break the ears of the bone, as much as you can, and then tie the ears of the bone, so that you can treat it more gently.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	If you do not once, if the bone is still wet until it is read, then take it out, because the extraction hurts.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	If the dislocation of the bone is against what we have said in the chapter, then do not follow what we have said; and prepare for incision on the nerve and vein, and make an incision according to how you will treat the arrowhead when it comes out, whether slowly or quickly, or firmly or elementally; and make the physician according to the shape of the arrowhead that was inside, because it is the greatest help that can be given, and if you do not follow what they tell you, then they will show you the sign.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	The first line translates to: "The arrow that came from another part, whether it opened anything of his, or the skin is compressed in some place where one can see or feel it: then pull it out as far as the prongs can hold, and then extract it: if it jumps now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is held in the bone, if you turn your round hand around as much as possible when it enters the bone, and widens the bone, then extract it.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	And if it cannot be drawn out, if you leave it alone, and then continue the extraction as much as possible when it draws back; and if it is the arrowhead and it is in the instrument, if the arrowhead enters the instrument's hair, and the instrument points at the end of the arrowhead, then pull it out, and if the arrowhead is in the hair, and the instrument point enters it, to lighten the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the arrow is buried, then it is necessary that you cut through the entire arm or remove the poison, and then cure the wound as best as possible.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if the arrow is stuck in the chest, belly, or abdomen, and it is protruding, then you must cut it out, and then pull it out slowly; and be careful not to cut the vein or nerve, and then extract it, and then clean the wound as much as possible, and continue the cure until it is healed.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the spikes used to treat arrows resembles the beak of an owl, and it looks like this:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are several ways to do it: large, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the arrowhead.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape of the pointed nail is like that of a bird's feather, inserted at the tip of the arrowhead, just as shown in this figure.
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	The form of the nails to be driven and pulled out is as follows:
des voinnes dou cors communes	common veins of large size.
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	There are 31 veins that are safe to cut, of which the largest is XVI, which is located after the ears, called the two "herbech" arteries; and the other two arteries located in the temples; and the veins located in the temples of the eyes, called "aspires"; and the vein located at the front of the head; and the vein located at the chief of the nose; and the gingers located at the collar; and the veins located in the lips of the mouth, called the "augeherich" veins; and the veins located below the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	The first sentence to translate is: "Les voinnes dont on saine communément sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composté de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.
