Those who have a cold complexion, if they sweat honey syrup, and aromatic wine that is between winter and spring, and consume little, and consume pungent foods and thin oils and pickles and juices; and when they start to sweat, they must drink more than usual; and it is necessary to give some men once a triaicle or muscate before the ventosacion, or afterward, to comfort the principal members; and it should be done subtly, but only those who are chilled by drinking.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	1. The wounds that are made to be felt are those that are made in the liver, and in the spleen, and gout, and in the stomach and bowels and bladder and hips, because this member does not suffer much pain from wounds, and only feels it when there is pain in one part of the body, as we do with our breasts when we are sick; to remove viscosity that is in the member, as we remove wounds from the stomach and bowels to soothe the member; and to relieve the pain when it has opilliation or piercing, if it is relieved by its own attraction of opilliation, or if it is lacking in piercing from the limb; and they are made when they are placed in the liver and in the spleen when there is retained viscosity, and these wounds are administered empty to suck only; and never are they administered together with fire, and never with hot aqua tede, as in diseases of the pleurisy, and in this manner we fill the wound with hot water, or with water that has been cooked with herbs.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the forceps administered by fire is:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	The form of the forceps administered by fire is: It has two sides of palm width and half, and has a cost on either side of the petite pertus, like a needle, and is made of iron or copper, so that it does not pierce the patient's skin when putting it in the member; and in the middle, there is a groove of iron or copper, for a spring to be placed, and there are large and small ones according to the diseases and age of those who take them, because the forceps of children are different from viels, and thin than fat.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	1. And it must be set on the wound of the member: take the cork or liniment, and put it in the wound through the handle that is in the wound, so that the cork or liniment is at the end of the wound where it does not burn the patient; then put it on the member, and you must be as we have said, if you see, if there is vapor, and if you take the wound; and take the liniment as before, and renew it often, if you can.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	1. In the wound that is maintained in a sickle-shaped cough, with no veins or bubbles, and is only made when it is clear of cough, and is put on the member only when it is clear of cough; and this is the form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	1. Withouts are not stolen except in parts where it is not possible to put ventouses due to their smallness, such as the lips and genitals, and similar parts; and in these parts withouts are removed by cutting, if it is not possible or not, and other similar things; and the quality of the user is that when you find withouts that are in soft waters, if you take them; you put them in a soft water bath, as long as they are family-like, and have no bellies; then it is healthy for the vein and the ventouse, then clean the member as much as it is red, and put on the withouts; and when they are smooth and look good, if it is the knee or the elbow, you put it on, because this is after.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	If not, then lift the leg of the wound, and then the limb; and if the patient is healthy too soon after the surgery, then take cold linen and wrap it around the wound, and put it on as long as the wound is bleeding; and if the wound bleeds more, then take hot vitrol or galls, and similar things, until it stops bleeding; or you can cut the leg in half of the dead flesh, and leave them as long as they are charred on the leg, until it is now healed; and if you have more time, then take other dead flesh.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And if the wounds do not take on their dressing, if you cleanse the limb with cold water, or you thread an needle as long as it does not soak, and then sew them in, and as they feel the sand, if they ache; and when you see that they are healing, if you powder some aloe and silk cloth, or charcoal, if they now burn.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	This is the beginning of the book of fractures.
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and it is the restoration of fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	You should know, dear friend, that this chapter is not without its merits, as there are no ancient books or letters that mention it; and for this reason, the science has been neglected in our land, because I have never found any book on the subject; and I do not know if anyone else has, except perhaps through the science of ancient books, or by my own study of the science, and by experiment, and by the custom of my life; and I have described in this chapter what is contained in it, and summarized it at the end, and shown clearly the shapes of the strangulations that are mentioned, as I have done in these two previous chapters.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is therefore necessary that we say at the beginning of this book the words and chapters or the sayings where one puts their understanding, and they measure the truth, so that those who have experienced it may learn this noble art, and they teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	I say that when there is a fracture, dislocation, torsion, or twisting, and it comes to any part of the body, if nothing else helps, then it is like a weak man, or child, or old woman; or if you hold it tightly, it is too tight, or too loose; and if you loosen it too much, it is to know that the cold joints, and the shoulders and elbows, and do not drink cold drinks, nor eat thin soups, nor fill the veins with blood, as long as you have no doubt of apoplexy, or expansion of matter in the member; if the patient improves under the same government that he has used.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	When the bones begin to heal, if it comes to passing through the patient's meat that makes a large wound, or if it is viscous, like dough that rises and cracks, and tests, and pies, and pancakes made of wool, and cheese, and fresh fish, and large wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For the healing wound becomes less painful and the fracture is sooner healed.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And you advise that fractures of the bones and degenerations are not well recovered or healed according to their nature by the growth of the limbs, and those who are too flexible, like the bones of small children; but if it is a large bone that is broken and jointed with the member, as much as it was before, and does not return to its former shape, and does not heal due to large meats, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And you know that fractures come in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fracture of the skull is different from that of the leg or arm, and I will tell you all kinds of fractures in this chapter.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there is a fracture that goes from the top of the skull, and another that is slicing, like the size of a quill to write.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if there is a fracture with a wound, and a small cut.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	And each fracture has its own engine and tool in restoration, according to what remembrance comes to the patient's mind; and the fracture of the bone is by that which is twisted, and wide open by defuire, and some are pressed by the hand; and if it is not twisted or frenched, and the pain is not great in the malady, there is no fracture, but there may be twisting or frenching or small fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	If you can only manage to move it with your hand, but use the medicines that will come later, and then the dislocation will be treated subtly.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	And you should be aware of the fracture that will occur in the shoulder, and the two parts that are separated should be reunited as soon as possible, unless it causes death; and if it causes death, then leave it alone until the pain subsides, and then gently and wisely put it back in place and realize that the restoration of the shoulder is lighter than the restorations of other bones or pieces; then the dislocation, if it can be done after this.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	When there are broken pieces in the bone of the foot, if they are two parts, it is hands or fingers, or in your hand, it is some small members, or in the tendons, or in one tendon and in your hand; and put the member according to its natural figure, so that when the parts of the broken member are adjusted, if you reset by your own efforts the additions in their place in the muscles that you please, and keep that by your effort does not cause the surgeon's injury or pain; and adjust well the two heads of the bones according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And it feels good in your hand if it seems that it is not well: if it curves beautifully and is not strained too much, do not press as those who come by their own effort cause the aposteme chaut and contraction of the member, as we have wanted many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And when the member is at its limit, if the patient well holds the shoulder that it does not move, neither by watching nor sleeping, nor turning, nor otherwise; and it is well that the member be firmly held so that it does not feel any pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	For when it feels no pain, if it is not at its limit, and it is necessary to put the member in a proper position so that it does not feel any pain; and hold it firmly so that twisting does not occur when it is restored; and the quality of the broken limb is according to what I will tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	It is said that the broken limbs are of different sizes in smallness and breadth and form.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	1. For the patient has lost limbs, just like you have lost your teeth and similar parts: if it happens to wrap cloths of fine linen and silk; and those that are large, if it is like a wide and hard rope, because the wide ropes tighten all the large member, and draw it evenly, unless it has no joint; then it wraps light and loose bands three or four times around the member, and holds the hand tightly along the entire rope, then goes to the end of the break and tightens it less than the break does, because the break only slightly widens the break; and softens the rope a little at a time, until you have taken a large part of the healthy skin, then take another rope, and turn the end towards the broken part, and tighten it gently, not too much or too little, as we said in the first part of the break; then go between the loose ends of linen or silk, until they are even, and then tie everything with a good knot, and then put your beads well made on, if it has not become inflamed or swollen.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	And if it has been struck or infected, if he puts on something soothing for the infected part and that relieves the pain, and leaves it alone for some time; then straighten your eyes, and they should be of a width of one and a half fingers' breadth, or of a sharp edge like a knife, or of the rains of palm, and they should be according to this figure:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	However, it is necessary that the one who puts on the wound make it larger and wider than the others; and it should be as long as the member of small or large size; then straighten your eyes in the same way as you did at the first session, then tie a thread around it, as you did at the first session, but not too tight; and the thread should be moderate, neither too thick nor too thin, and should be of linen; for if the thread is too thick, as I have seen the works of fools who make their knots with linen threads, it is a great mistake, for the wound cannot be even if it is too fine, and it is only necessary that there be less than an inch between each eyelet;
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is found by the helpers after the castration of the males, if they are not clean, then they should put on clean linen or cloths, so that they do not get sick.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with the bandage, and the edges are torn, I will tell you the treatment for this after.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And be careful not to strain too much on all the broken limbs in the first hour.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	For when the limbs are large, it is not advisable to put them in bandages immediately, but rather after V hours or VII, or according to your skill in plastering; and here is the way of the old plasters to restore fractures, dislocations, and torsion: and that you take flour that is between the mills, and knead it with a great deal of beer, and make this dough, neither too thick nor too thin, and use it, and this is the common way of restoring fractures in other positions, and even in women and children, because it is not too tight or too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana V З.; alechil VIIII З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	1. Another way to mend fractures and dislocations and twists: take barley and linseed and oil and Arabian gum and gum, in the ratio of 1:10; mix with aloes, in the ratio of 1:5; alechil, in the ratio of 1:7; and make a powder, and mix with cow dung; if the complexion of the face is hot, use this plaster as it is of good composition and restores fractured bones quickly, and is beneficial to many men.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	1. Another way to relieve twisting: take gum and vismallow, in the ratio of 1:10; mix with aloes, in the ratio of 1:5; acacia, in the ratio of 1:3; arsenic, in the ratio of 1:2; and dry well, and cook with vinegar or cow dung, and administer.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Other ways to use the plaster on joints and bones, and ease the pain coming, and the wounds use of the bone: take new cloth, and the oil and butter cooked, and put it on the leg.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	These plasters do not restore the skin, but they are useful for easing the pain of inflammation, and properly treating bone pain.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another way to make the plaster that restores broken bones: take dry fig leaves and earth pottery, and blend them together, and make the plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another way to make the plaster for the restoration of bone fractures and to reduce inflammation.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	The root of vismalve, chamomile, violet flowers, flour of quince, each part; and boil, and infuse with wine, and wash the members, and apply with fresh coriander water or wine, or with water, and use.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another way to emplace more forcefully than the first, when an abscess comes to the restoration of the member.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Boil the roots of vismalve, and the linseed, balm, honeybee, and sansuce, and violet and chamomile flowers, each part; and boil, and infuse with fresh salt water or sweet water, or with wine, according to the choler of the member, and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	In his book, Ypocras states that no material is used to set a broken bone for restoration, and nothing else, and he says that it should be neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	It seems that Galen suggests that when setting a broken bone for restoration, one should use dry things like hot mirrors and aloes, incense, and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another way to treat injury and pain: take fresh and clean pork fat, or the feathers of geese, and apply it, and the wounds, and the bandages, and then cover the limb.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then a little later, take care that the patient's shoulder does not feel any pain or stiffness in the bones of his arm; if it does not happen by hand, and pain comes to the shoulder, or itching, tingling, or swelling, if you haste, and reduce it, and now press the dressing; take a light fold, a wet sponge, plunge in cold water, and lift the limb as long as the itching ceases and the pain subsides; then let the member rest for an hour, then put on a dry cloth, moisten with cold or rose oil, and tie with a knot, as you are sure not to be afraid of gangrene; allow the inflammation in the member to subside, and the pain to cease, then resume gentle pressure, a little empress, and do not strain it too much; gently as long as it is healthy.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	If you see that the wound is bleeding, swollen, painful, and inflamed, and you have the skill to plaster and dress it, if it recurs, as you did at first, in the same manner.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	If you do not see any sign of this that we have said, if it does not occur after three days or four or seven; and never more than twenty days, according to what one sees, as long as the wound is broken and approaches the chariot; therefore, a stronger restraint, and the flesh grows larger, as I have said before; and if you see the flesh drying up more than it should, be careful that no one comes; take care of the warm water, every time you wet it, and keep a little fire going; by this means, you will cut off the norrissemens at the member, and mend what they do to the flesh, so that the member is tortured: this is harmful, and if it is not treated with care, and I know no other way than to be gentle and treat it fairly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	Of various wounds of breaking
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	There are many kinds of wounds of breaking, and different figures, and the causes are assigned; for there are wounds made by the collision of a spear, and the whole bone is fractured as if it were a hazel or thistle; and therefore this kind of breaking is called «hazel-breaking».
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	Or the spear strikes the bone through its various senses and is called this kind of breaking "absolute"; and it is the wound of these two great or small fractures.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if it has a collision embedded, or pierced or of the collar of the wound, or of the cheek against the wound, or of other such things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a persistent fracture, which approaches the skin that is exposed to the bone, or it is under the bone, and this wound or large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if there is a wound that is reset in the bone just as subtle as a thorn, and it is a small cut, and for this it is called this fracture "capillary"; and if the wound that is made by hurting the piercing, or by tearing, or by something else, and makes the piece of the bone enter, and it is the same as when they set the caustics when they were heated on the caustics; if it enters the pierce.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	1. And this happens more often among those with wet bones, just like children's bones; and it occurs in all these ways of fracture that are lightly broken, just like these; and I will speak about it in their language.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	2. And let us know all ways of fractures by the removal they cause, and the inquiries made, and by the corrupted char that is caused.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	3. The apparent appearance is known by the fact that when one discovers the bone, and rubs it with oil, if the dark fracture is not open,
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	4. In the treatment of the fracture, keep a close watch on the patient's condition, and if you see no serious accidents, such as vomiting of clear liquid, admission of understanding, extension, and pulselessness, and fever, and the wounds becoming red and swollen, and other signs of serious conditions that cannot be cured with doubt,
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	If you do not see an unexpected accident, and you hope for a cure, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	When the first pain comes to you, and it is in the shoulder, if it is necessary to break the bone before the fourth month of pregnancy, then do so.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	If it is in this way, and you have already broken the bone before the ninth month of pregnancy, then the tendon around the bone must be rotten, and the accident we have mentioned will occur.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	If the bone fracture comes at the end of the tendon that covers the eye, then it is necessary to cut off the damaged part: and if you prescribe the salve of the new mother's wound, and open the bone in all the ways you can, and show the figure of the wound more severe than you can, and if the sand comes out to discover the bone, or the pus comes out, if it helps that it happens, and if you fill the wound with oiled powdered silk; and rest the wound as long as the pus is stopped and is sure of not coming out, and then begin to break the bone, and it is done according to twenty ways of cutting: one way is when you cut at the end that is narrow before, and it is in this form.
Et puis i boute I autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then, another joint of greater size than the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second method is if you have many types of joints, some pointed and others wide, and they are sharp, and are made of iron; and you perform them lightly, so as not to wound the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is hard and thick, then you must perforate it with care, otherwise you will injure the joints with toothpicks. Instead, use small pieces of wood or bone that do not penetrate further into the bone than necessary, and have a margin or circle around them that does not allow the tip to pass over the bone. And you must have more of these, so that each one fits the size of the bone, if you have toothpicks for every test; and this is the form of the three methods of toothpicks:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	1. To determine the quality of the break in the bone, you put your thumb on the bone, and turn it until you feel that the bone is perceived; then place your thumb on the other part a little later, and do the rest, then cut through the end of the bone that is between the holes, and do it as subtly as you can, and lightly, as we have said, as you draw the bone with your hand, or with any of the instruments you have, like needles, tweezers; and make sure you do not touch the skull or the face.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	2. When you have perceived and cut the bone, and if you find that the suture is tightened by the bone to all other instruments like a knife, but it should be looser and more subtle than the other knife; and if it does not tighten any small bones, nor any scales, if the light bones are gently with the instruments we have said; then cure the wound with stitches and staples that we have mentioned.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And the other way of opening is when it is more like that of the Galians, who are safer; and the lock is very tight, and it is their word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary to first remove a part of the bone, where the fracture is open, so that when you have removed this part, measure from the top of the chief of this incisor lenticular, and it will be in this form:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	And do not cut too much, and the piece is turned in two pieces, if the cutting is towards the bone; then with a small saw, if you lightly touch the bone all around, and be well prepared for the thread that is outside; if it is near the bone, if the bone is light, because it is well understood that it is harmful to the bone, and it causes pain.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	If the bone fracture does not pierce through the skin, and the bone is only cracked, and it has small pieces, if they cover that roughness, and smooth out the scales with the subtle grater that you must have several quantities of, to adjust each joint according to the severity and shape of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you rub before with coarse graters, and after with more subtle ones, and continue doing this until it is well.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other hair removal and subtle fracture, it is necessary to adjust according to its address; and this is something that cannot be answered by the one who has studied in this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	1. If the facial injury is discovered, then it is necessary to apply linen dipped in oil to the wound, according to the size of the wound, and place a second layer of doubled linen on top, dipped in wine and olive oil, and placed over the first layer; and make this more gently than you please, so as not to burn the face, then apply other linen layers, and do not strain it too much, only as much as it covers the wound; and leave it on for one or two days, until the swelling is subsided, then remove it, and apply medicines such as rue, flour, salt, incense powder, and aristolochum, and similar things; and from these things make a powder, and apply it to the wound, and apply subsequent medicines without burning; and ensure that the wound is clean, so that you do not leave the ointment or assemble bowels, because when bowels are assembled under the skin, they can cause great harm to the patient; for if something mordant is placed on the face, it can cause great pain.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	When none of the patients have accidents come to the physician, if we have said so, then there is doubt about the sense of doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the black is only brought by medicine that has been given, then a part of honey, and three parts of rose oil, and one part of glue, and put on the face; then the cure is done in the ways of cures that it covers, as long as it is healthy.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Wise men who have never broken the two parts of the nose, or one only, because they are bones; and this is also cartilaginous, and does not break, unless it is bent or twisted, and then it becomes healthy.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	If one of the two parts is broken, then if you can reach your small toe or finger hole, and make the break even with your index finger, and in the pouch as long as it does not deviate from its natural figure; and do this lightly, and make sure that the patient does not feel pain through your touch.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	If the break is in the part of the nail, and cannot be reached by the toe, then if you can put it even with the head of a large pin in the palm,
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	If the break is in the second part, then if you repeat it, and restore the first joint, if possible; if not, after the ninth or tenth time, when the wound is calmed, then reach for the head of the nail with your thumbs, if the break is in a different part.
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	When you cut into another part, if the wound is large; and let the tents be as large as they fill the cavities without causing pain.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And no restaurer would say that one must soften the tents with burrs, and each year.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	It seems to me that this is indeed the best, but it must be made soft in the construction of oven ashes and ground bone powder; then leave the tent, as long as the bone is hard, and the cartilage is hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And never cut on the wings of tents, and if it is soft and hanging, and holds the bracelet, and blows the medicine among; or do as you have seen.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en I poc de dyaquilon.	If the abscess bursts during the operation, and you do not clean it with oil or fine linen, or in a vessel of wine, it will cause great harm.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the abscess does not burst during the operation, and you cover it with ointment made of flour of eggs and incense powder, mixed with fresh milk, then put on light cloths, and do not close the wound; and if the wound is small, and it is torn into thin pieces, if you can find suitable bandages for it, then wrap it up, and treat the other wounds with ointments and plasters, and sutures, as suitable ointments and plasters are for this; and if there is no sign of infection in the wound, then cure it with splints, and put on bandages, as long as it is healthy.
de la routure de la mandibule	Of the dislocation of the lower jaw
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the lower jaw is dislocated, there is no wound, and the fracture is not deep, but rather a slight one, not breaking into pieces, only slightly, and not as deep as a cone.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	It is necessary, if the fracture is on the left side, to place your index finger in the mouth of the patient; and if the fracture is on the right side, then place your index finger on the left hand, lightly press the break, and the injury is treated with the other hand, and it is held firmly.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en II, si covient que tu aministres extension de II pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the fracture of the lower jaw is described as a second degree, then it comes that you administer extension to two parts, as long as they are equal.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if the teeth move or fracture, or if they are torn from a gold, silver, or silk thread, then they should be inserted into the broken lower jaw fragment, and one double cloth strip should be placed; and a well-made iron nail or a piece of leather should be placed along and across the lower jaw according to its length, and it should be tied to the mouth that you use, and the patient should be commanded to lie down, and light foods should be given.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	1. If you see that the limb is twisted, if it does not return to its place within three days, then reset it to where it was originally; then apply a plaster made from flour of the mill with as much urine or flour of sinew as you can stand; after which, apply a lighter plaster, and when it adheres, the dislocation will not change again, leave it as it is until it is healthy; it will be healthy many times in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	2. If the wound becomes infected, if you do not follow what we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	3. If there is a fracture and wound together, cut out a small piece of bone; if the bone is flexible enough to be bent.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	If the wound is large, then enlarge it according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus I des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When you have all these pieces and there is no need to enlarge the wound, if it is large, then make sure to cover it with flexible bandages at this time, in order to heal quickly and become healthy.
de la forcele	of its strength.
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The force breaks more often in front of the shoulder, towards the elbow, and the break is in three ways: it is broken and split into two, with two pieces, and it is lighter to restore; or it is broken with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	The patient should be examined if there is pain at the site of injury, and if the other end of the bone is swollen, indicating forceful impact; then extend the collar towards the affected area, and place the fracture in your hands so that it forms as intended, ensuring no deformity or instability.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	If you are more skilled at extension, place the shoulder blade of the patient on the table, and wrap a round or flat object around it according to your needs; then gently apply force, and hold the sphere in your hand, ensuring that the fracture is placed accurately and as intended.

When you do not treat the head of the strong force as soon as it is injured, because it comes in front, it can cause the patient to lose consciousness and put their hand on their chest or ear, and hold their shoulder and elbow with both hands until the bone of the strong force is raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	And then address the fracture to your two hands, and if you break the fragments, it can happen that you lose them; and try to pull out the light pieces, and if the bone does not join by any means with any projection, if it is at one of the incisions you made; but that you hold the strong force instrument tightly to warn for the face:
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	And it seems like a spoon, and is not too thin, and should be as wide as the bone wants, according to the size of the bone and the strength of the muscle; and if there are two heads, as you see, and some are large, and others are narrow, if it is the rupture of the wound that you made when you treated the bones, and when you are sure of the rupture, if the wound is small, or you doubt the rupture, if you use the wound with linen and bandages, according to its quantity.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille I drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if aphrodisiacs are used and come, if many oils are mixed with rosewater and alcohol, and it is applied.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	1. The splitting of the bone is when it feels pain and seems too small, you must then powder the fine flour and honeybeeswax, and lightly sprinkle it on, and place a lead ball at the bottom; if you have the means, then take a very large palm leaf, and double-fold the towels, and press them down; then take a thin slip of three inches wide and long, and wrap it around the bend, so that the bend's ends are held down; and place the slip on the wrist, and turn the bend at the wrist, and tighten the slip on the healthy bone, and tighten the sick bone as well, and loosen the bend at the wrist, and when you see that the bend holds the break, and you see clearly that the slip does not move along the broken bone, if it rewards each time, and when it tightens, so that you can lift the injured arm; and make the malice on the back of the malaide, and place it when it falls asleep on the wrist, to raise the helper up; if you align the break with the alignment of the shoulder blade, or if you put the arm at the collarbone, and it does not slip out of place accidentally, then within 20 days, then resume the pressing, if you see that it has use, and hold it and let it go as soon as it is restored; and it is restored in 28 days, and in no fewer than any number of men.
de la brisure de l’espaule	Of the fracture of the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement. de la brisure dou pis	of the break
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	The bone is never broken in the field, but it happens sometimes; but it often breaks at the defense.

de la brisure dou col	Of the fracture of the shoulder

de la brisure de l’ajutoire	Of the shoulder dislocation
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The shoulder is the bone that lies between the neck and the shoulder blade of the arm, and if it is dislocated, then it must be restored according to one of the following two methods:

Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.
