Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If the address, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	And if no such accidents occur, it is only after three days or more, and the patient lies down on his back, and has his hands on his stomach; and put the help in place with plain linen evenly, and look at every hour of the day or night, when the broken bone does not move, or is not softened by the ligaments; if it is due to the power of medicine, and the meat that we have before us, in such a way that the meat is subtle; and when it comes to be taken back, if it is large.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	And it is customary that the helper and the leg are returned in 40 days or more; therefore, they should be wrapped and given baths and remedies for the joints to strengthen the limb.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	And if the stricture is thick and tight, it should be undone every few days or up to two months.
de la brisure du bras	of the arm fracture
Li bras est compos de II os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is composed of two bones, which are called the "humerus" and the "ulna," where one is shorter and the other is longer; and they are connected by the elbow; by chance, only one of the long bones breaks, or the short one, or both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	When the little bones are broken, the restorations are light, and the cures; and when the great ones are broken, if it is a poor cure, and more wounded than when they were broken separately.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If it is only the little bones that are broken, then it will be necessary to lightly extend and put equal.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	And if it is the great bones, then it will be necessary to strain more strongly; and extend it over the little finger, and raise the palm of the hand higher than the others, and the feet lower, and let the malice be on itself, and the little finger higher, so that the malice suffers no labor; then extend the other arms to the part opposite the hand, or to the elbow, and some other arms to the other side.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And then he puts it in its place, according to its better form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if it is broken into pieces, then he puts each piece in its place, and if there are no loose teeth that point towards the knee, and you cannot restore it to its place, then as we have said before, this is a serious matter.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if with the fracture there is a wound, I have spoken to the individual surgeon; if he takes care of it.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	And if in the beginning of restoration there arise postoperative swelling, if the dressing made of olive oil and lead-based wax is not too hard or too soft, but subtle, until the swelling is pacified.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	Then take the ointment, and put the powder of the mill with a lot of urine on it, then put the sticks, and let the wreath be larger than the others; and see if there are VI sticks or arms in more positions: whether the wreath is in one of the bones, or in two; and draw it more under the wreath than elsewhere, as I said at the beginning of this chapter; and let the moisture that is under the wreath be soft and not hard or sharp; and let the strings, which are drawn out, be of linen, neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And reward the member and the ligament after some years.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	And if any accidents come to the member, if it is like itching to the member, then you must apply hot water to the member as long as the itching is relieved; and let the member rest in peace.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And then the inflammation resumes, and if the ligaments are loosened and the bones are broken, it seems like something, if it is addressed.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses I poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if the wounds cannot come to the member because it is too tight, because it is too tight, then you must loosen it in a short time, and let it rest for some years, until the wounds are healed, and then the member will be stretched.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	And if none of these things come to the patient in XX years, it is not good.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	If the dislocation is not reduced, then the patient can move their hands to their collarbone, and it should be even, and they should be still and quiet, and sleep on their back; and it is hoped that this reduction is restored in XXX years or XXXV, and by chance in XX years, according to the compositions and complexions of the virtues.
de la brisure de la main	of the wrist dislocation
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Wishes that on the back of the hand and in the two wrists there are few dislocations, and only twisting many times.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en I drapeil de lin.	1. And when the plant of the hand is broken or twisted, if it is found that the patient's hand has a correct angle, and it stands straight in front of him; then he places his hand on the extended nail, extends the fingers of the broken bones, and puts them evenly in the holes, as long as they are well joined; then he applies plaster and stitches, if necessary, then he puts an elephant on according to the quantity of the nail; and it is wrapped in a gutter of linen.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	1. And if the fracture is at the sides of the belly of the plant, then make a gauze ball, and instruct the patient to stretch it on his broken plant; then stretch from a long gauze, and it should be as large as the plant of the hand, and it is stretched, if it can be done.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the fracture is at the elbow, then it comes that you place an splint on, and another on the plant, if the hand is over and straight, then the arm is fully tightened, and the line between the two is stretched.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en I tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And if the fracture does not come to either of us, if it is bent, then if it is held straight, as it should; and the tightened with the plant, and if you see that a splint is placed right and small on the wrist to lift the fracture, and it does not move; and if the fracture is in other parts, such as the index finger or one of the others, if it is held straight, and the other is held with the healthy finger that follows; or you hold them all together, as much as possible, or you place a splint on it, as it should; and be careful in the restoration and the disposition of the wound, and what comes, as I said.
de la cuixe brisie	Of the broken vessel
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie I liien desus la briseure, et I autre desoz.	The bone of the vessel is often broken, and it can be seen when it turns forward and backward; the restoration is if the ligaments that support the fracture are tightened and the other one is loosened.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And the patient suffers from pain in their face, then each part extends its ligaments according to its own, and it is when the fracture is complete.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if the fracture is close to the root of the vessel, then some of the ligaments are pulled towards the point of pain, and the others are loosened at the fracture.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	And as it has reached the bone, and therefore the bone's length, and the bone's extension; then place the bones equal with your two hands, according to its natural figure, and then place the template, and the bone, and if it does not move, it is correct.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if it does not move, let it rest for a while and return to your care and the cure; the wound is made in part.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	It is necessary that you wrap the wound with a bandage doubled in width of II or III, and remove any excess, then bend the leg so that the heel comes to the root of the nail, and put the long piece between the thigh and the leg, leaving the knee bare; then bend the leg and the thigh again with the bandage, and put on the bandage again, and place an estile on the bone of the leg; then put leather between the leg and the thigh to fix the string, then start to tie for form III or IV on the bandage; and as you add more layers of the bandage, the less it is tightened; then take out the two ends of the thread that you have tied between the leg and the thigh, and in the three estiles that are fastened, then return to the knee of the thread, until you see the pit; the string, if it does not move from its place, then let it alone, then leave it, then it will not move anymore, neither apostheme nor enfleure.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	If it happens, if it leaves, and addresses what comes, as we have said many times; and if there are pieces of bone that prick, if they can be found, then it is possible; and if not, then it may be necessary to cut the limb and drain it; and the cure, as we have said, depending on how healthy it is.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And never has the hip been broken otherwise than when one sets it in place, as we have seen in the shoulder and arm; however, in the restoration that has been made, it does not clash with the patient's pain.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en L jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And you advise that the hip is restored in a short time, or at least a little more, according to the differences in complexion.
de la ruelle dou genoil	Of the right knee joint
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	It is said that in the right knee joint there are few breaks, but it bends many times.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	And if it breaks, whether it is only a fracture or a puncture, and comes to all wounds, and feels pain, and that is not good.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is when you put back in place whatever has been dislocated as much as possible, and then put on the plaster, and if you have a roller, and roll it around, as you can, then tighten as you should, then reward all the positions we have said for other dislocations, such as the popliteal fissure and other similar ones; if you put on the plaster for each accident as much as is possible, then it should be healthy.
de la brisure de la jambe	Of the break of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	It is said that in the leg there are two bones, and some are called by right "mustelz", and the others are called "foscile"; and all fractures are similar to those of the arm, and for this it is the restoration as well as the arm properly, and the parts are all. And if the two bones are broken together, then turn the leg from all sides.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the delicate bones are broken, then turn forward.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz.	And if the large bones are broken, then feel great pain and see that it is well; then turn slowly.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	The patient must extend the limb and hold it evenly; however, it is important to note that if the fracture is crooked, and there are more pieces, then the extension should be smaller and lighter; and the alignment according to your strength.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren II faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have completed your work, if you take two strips of wool threads that are purple and run along the leg on both sides, and are long enough to cover the leg from the groin to the ankle, then wrap them around the leg and tie it tightly, and at this point do not let the leg sway to the right or left, and it is well; and no one increases the pain of the leg, and it is made of flax, and I put it on the leg to watch for movement, and properly made it in the fracture or wound; and shake each leg every day to see if there is any swelling or other accident; if the cure is as soon as it is healthy.
de la brisure des os dou piet	Of the break of the bones of the shoulder
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle, there is no break, but the bones of the shoulder never break and must be very hard, and they have only been broken in more positions.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a II chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if the bones of the shoulder are broken and you see the bones sliding over each other, if you put them on the ground as hard as possible, just like when you are flying, then put your hand on the shoulder and lift the bones as much as they can; then press them until they return to their place; then put the splint and stitch it, and put a small pillow under the chest of the shoulder, then draw it towards the shoulder joint, then wrap the rest of the clothes around it, and other things that you have skill for.
Et quant III jors ou IIII seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	When three or four days have passed, if the bone is not healed, you will find the bones uneven, broken, and dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	If there are two breaks, if they heal, as we have said, the hand must be set; then put a splint on the other end according to the length of the bone; and make a pad for the joint that I have mentioned, and make it wider; and if there are two or three, or more, breaks, if you put one on each end according to its quantity, wrapped in a single layer of linen, and tighten the joint around the padding; and let the hand be placed so that the elbow is over the stomach of the joint, so that it is well tanned.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	It is necessary that you do not ignore the other things I have said for other fractures, as soon as we have said them; and treat each accident in the same way that is necessary.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the bone break of the shoulder
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the woman's shoulder bone is broken, if it is made to fit, then it inclines towards the part of the shoulder, and is held by the hand; then fill the nature of the maim with cloth, and put it in as much as it can hold; then lift the woman, and gently bend the shoulder a little at a time, until the cloth comes to the entrance of the nature, and returns the bone with the cloth; and if she sees blood, if the cloth is soaked, and if she has been soaked, put it back on, and in seven days or more: if the fracture is restored, and if you see it, take a bowl of water, and tie a string around the hole, and blow all the water into the nature; then suck out of the string, until the bowl is empty: the nature will return to the fracture; then fill it with cloth, and leave it alone for several days, until it is healthy.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	When the bone of the elbow is broken, or of the female, if it is repaired as we have said in the elbow of the horse; and these fractures are not hidden that are near to him who sets his study and his use, and reads my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	For the fracture means in more ways the right direction of the restoration: understand the doubts.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse III jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In the joint, when it is broken, take an ostrich's beak and bite the joint; then wrap it with cloth, and leave it for three days or so, and it will heal quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	Of a fracture with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for the one who has a fracture with wound, even if it is large, as the bone of the shoulder or elbow, or seeming, that it be healthy now, if that wounds which we have said testify.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the healthy wound is, if the cauterization of vitrol, if you have nothing else, then resume to restore the fracture in the same hour, or the next day, if the patient does not come.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if the cauterization is done and the patient comes, if you leave the restoration for the next day, as long as the cauterization is calmed, and do not touch it again on the third or fourth day, because you will make the patient come to accident.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the bone breaks, it is exposed on the side of the knee discovered, so it comes that you put it lightly in your hands, at a small extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a VII dois ou VIII de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne III ou IIII, selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the extension is not apparent for you to put it evenly in your hands, then the splint that is of iron, which is seven or eight inches long, and the width is according to the size of the wound; and for this, it is a matter of practice that he pierces three or four, according to how many there are in each case of setting the fracture; and it should be thin and a large one, which does not crush the compression on the member of your hand, and it should also be in front, and a large one in front, in this way:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	The term "palainche" refers to a type of bandage or dressing used in medieval medicine. The text states that it is used when the headbones (cranial bones) need to be set, and the bone ends are aligned so that they fit together like a puzzle piece. Once the bone ends are properly aligned, the dressing is applied, and the patient is left to rest until the bone heals.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	If the fracture is subtle, and the fragments cannot be easily grasped by the bone, it is necessary to apply pressure to the head of the bone, as soon as the fragments have some mobility. This helps to reduce the risk of further injury and promotes healing.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	If you are unable to realign the bone, as we have previously advised, if it is held by an instrument suitable for this purpose, either a forceps or a knife, or a hook, then you must remove it from the bone as quickly as possible. This should be done with gentle pressure and minimal trauma to the surrounding tissues.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	When the bone is set, and the patient feels great pain afterwards, you should suspect that something is not right in its natural state.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	If you keep it in its natural state, and then apply a thin layer of black, unscented linseed oil, and properly do this; and do not put anything on the wound or other places where there is oil, so as not to cause rotting and corruption; then administer ointments as you restore the bone, and leave the wound exposed, covering it completely according to the size of the wound, and be sure that the wound does not become tight with the fracture; and many times have I seen this cause the patient's health to deteriorate, and have caused death or corrosion in no time; and the scars are softer and less yellow than those of other fractures.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	When the wound is large or severe, and you doubt that it will heal, as we have said, and you feel pain in the leg, but cannot put on bandages; then wrap the leg with cloth, make tight bandages, and tie them.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	When you see after the first or second day that the wound has become infected, and if all that you have applied has not helped to heal the wound, and if you use antiseptic remedies for painful wounds, as we have used in the past.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre II fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	It is necessary that you unwrap the limb twice a day, in the morning and evening, as long as it is swollen and healthy.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it is necessary that the limb is aligned in a certain way that the belly corresponds to the leg lightly.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if they continue to thrust, and it cannot be held but only moved away from the belly, with small pieces of bone, because it is necessary that you cover the wound with a tent, and all these pieces damaged that cause this pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if an abscess comes to the skin, or in some other way of corruption, and it is necessary that you treat it, according to what is said in this chapter before.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And when the bone is broken and exposed through the skin, as in the bone of the thigh or shoulder, and other similar bones of the large limbs, if it is not treated, because often death comes, but it is left until it perishes; by chance it may heal after 20 or 30 years, then treat the wound, if you can; and if you cannot, leave it.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	of thorns that come out of the heat
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	We come often after the health of the incision, in fact when it is near the joint, and it is a sad thing to see the member; and by chance cannot make the limbs their natural size.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	If the wound is fresh: if it is treated with stiptic medicines, such as aloes, incense, and myrrh, and sarcocolle, acacia, and other similar things, if you take none of these things or all together, and mix them with warm stiptic wine or with an abundance of urine or with vinegar; and then apply them to the wound in poultices, and draw it well out of the hands; and then withdraw it, and repeat another one, as long as the necrotic tissue is sound; or you pull out a well-made piece of plaster; for the property of the plaster is that it all cures the swellings in the members; and if the necrosis is already converted into firmness, and is like a piere, and it is easy to the bone, if the gauze is changed, and the superfluity is cut off; or you leave it without any raser, as long as it is sound, and the cure as long as it is healthy.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	The weak limb after imprisonment
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the bone fracture is healed and recovered, and subsides after the weak limbs and gently, if for any reason it comes from: of one it comes because it was cut too narrowly, and was not as it should have been; or because it received too many screws, and could not come to the member; or for a multitude of arthritis; or for too great movements, not in its hour; or because it has little blood in its chest, and is weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the cure if you make the patient drink honey and make the chest tense as much as possible without multiplying in it; and give him a bath, and he then becomes happy and calm; then put vinegar on the limb, if the swelling increases at great norrisment, and the arthritis often decreases, until the swelling corresponds to the member; and then return to its natural shape.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	The dislocated limb after the healing process.
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai I emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the limb is swollen after restoration, and the bone is openly broken, and the shape of the dislocated limb is deformed, it is not in its natural state: if one does not believe the fools who say that one must break the bone entirely, and all others have done this in our land; and these injuries are blamed, and great harm comes of it, and by chance the death occurs, however, if the wounds and tortures are fresh, and if they are washed with hot water or herbs that are mollifying are cooked, as cold compresses or roots, and such things; and I apply a mollifying ointment, as well made, and I take the mucilage of vismilk, and cook it with melted lard or olive oil, and apply it on; or I take fat figs and chew them with cinnamon, and such medicines that dry the sweat.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And no time is there where the node does not continue and long to touch with wet hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And let there be no movement in the limb every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the tortuosity is awakened and hardened, as well as the incision, and it needs to be healed with iron, then let it be coated with copper if it can reach the bone, through a subtle and light subtraction; and study and practice in the cure.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book of dislocations.
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation comes to none, if it comes now to bring sensation to the target.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	For if we delay, if it is not seen, and by chance if it is reset on the shoulder; because it cannot be moved to the ear where it is inflamed: many times come spasm and other pains; always, when this happens, I make the patient healthier, then leave it, as long as the feverish inflammation is calmed; then warm and oily oil is applied to the limb, then it is gently reset, and each member is cured as it was cured in its shoulder.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	I have ordered the surgeons for the dislocations of the shoulder joints.
des mandibules	for the mandibles
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc II manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	There are cases where the mandibles are dislocated, and the dislocations of the jaws are in two ways: either they are a small piece of their bones, and become softened; or they are completely dislocated, and hang downwards, and cut off the saliva from the mouth that cannot hold it, and cannot close the mouth, and envelops the tongue with the word.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, it returns through more positions.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	1. If it is complete and accomplished, if you reset it immediately and do not move it; in such a way that the surgeon marks the patient's head with the tool, and cuts one of his hands at the root of the dislocation of the mandible, which is the lower jaw, where the dislocation is located; and the other two hands are deflected, to make them equal; and instruct the patient to smooth and move all of them.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	2. And the teeth are placed in their place, as they should be in his jaw.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les II mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	3. If the jaw is reset, it should be done gently, that is, the lower and upper jaws together, as long as the teeth are not moved too much; and do not move them excessively, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	And when they are returned correctly, the patient's mouth feels well, then put soft cloths on it made of olive oil and wax, then lightly tie them with strings; let the patient sleep on his back, and his head between two pillows, so that he does not move to the left or right, nor strain himself, but gently feed him with meat as long as the pain is steady and does not affect the jawbones; then remove what he saw lightly, and do not try to open his mouth with his fingers and drink, as long as the jawbone is well healed and healthy.
Et se les II mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two lower jaws cannot be realigned at once and are not converted to their original position, and if fever and customary aches come, and by chance the stomach is affected, and by chance vomiting of clear bile.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en VIIII jors.	And when you see this, you will know that it is disastrous; and many have died in the past, in nine years.
de la forcelle	of force
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The force cannot be overcome with the cost of continued use, and it is never stable at the end, and it is well known that it is so.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And the restoration is when the patient bends at the waist and extends his arms; then press on the shoulder with your palm, and it will return; then place the splint and the bandage, and tighten them; and the part that is towards the shoulder cannot be realigned, but if it does not come back, then reset it at the shoulder as we have said, and then place the splint and the bandage, and tighten them, and command the patient to rest until he is healthy; and then again, bring the head of the dislocation back to its original position when the limb is released from the shoulder.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	Of the shoulder dislocation
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	There are three ways the shoulder can dislocate: either it dislocates at the shoulder blade area; or at the hip area; or at the elbow area, and that happens rarely; or it does not dislocate at all, but rather at the shoulder; and this happens more often in those with less strength, because they jump farther; in those with more strength, they jump a little, and then return.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And by chance, some men may experience trauma or fracture, and the shoulder is dislocated from an abscess, and make sure it is reset by this means.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	It is therefore necessary that you examine it, as long as you are certain; and then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	And it is known that dislocations occur when turned towards the axis, and there is a difference between the affected spine and the healthy one; you will find this difference manifestly; you will find at the head of the shoulder a hole, and then at the top of the shoulder the head of the shoulder, as if it were an "O"; and the patient cannot bring his hand to his side, nor move without any movement; and if it is dislocated upwards, if it is not hidden, because you can see it clearly at the top; and this way of dislocation is not easy to return, when it is new, or if the patient is a child.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	The manner is that the physician gently places his hand on the shoulder of the patient, then places his thumb under the acetabulum, and gently presses on the joint with his fingers at the top of the thigh; he then releases his hand and extends it upwards, placing it beside the patient; if it comes quickly.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	And if it does not come as we have said in our hands a short time after, then it is that the patient should be bathed in hot water; and the physician applies an ointment softening and soothing, as a decoction of aloe and fenugreek and honey in hot water, and is applied; then he soothes the patient on his back, and places one hand on the acetabulum at its lowest point, neither too soft nor too hard, then places the foot of the patient's leg on the hand, and gently presses the shoulder muscle, and traces the physician's hand; and other physicians trace the shoulder muscle if it does not move; this shoulder now returns, and you see if you follow this manner: and it is that you cause the present home to be larger than the shoulder; and it should be turned towards the chest, and should be placed on the shoulder of the physician, and gently lifted up, so that the shoulder hangs in the armpit; and other physicians trace the physician's hand from the shoulder towards the belly.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And if the patient is too weak, if it can with nothing heavy to do with it, then the dislocation returns now.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	And the reduction is also done in another way: and it is like this: take the long pin in the earth, of which the heads are also returned as the pistal, and not too big nor too rude; then place it on the patient's shoulder, but if it has been bent too much, and the shoulder is too long, then extend your hand from another part, and the joint returns to its place immediately; and if it does not return after all these things that we have said, then do this cure: take the pin of two forearms of large and medium size, which has the head entered from the front of the shoulder according to this form:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus I eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	Then lie the head of the nail that it was not bent by the surgeon, then put it in the hole of the nail; and extend some of the arms over the long nail, and the helper over the shoulder, and the arm at the wrist of another, then put the arm on the handle of an arrow, and stretch the hands apart from each other, and let the chest hang down from the other side: the joint was now fixed.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is done, in whatever way that may be, if you put the hole a linen thread even, then put the plaster of powdered flour with incense and urine on all the shoulder blade and ribs, then draw the nail through the hole again, and turn the line on the plaster, and bandage the hand on its collar, and the hand will remain still.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés V jors ou VII, et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And it is necessary that he drinks little at first, until the limb is comfortable, for it will heal faster; then gradually drink more after the first seven or eight days, and move it; and if it is tight and does not become soft, it is healthy.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint is tight due to moisture or for another reason, it is necessary that you administer cauterization at three pulsations, as it is placed before or in the chapter of cauterizations.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés VII jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do all this, and after seven weeks, the joint does not hold and cannot raise the arm forward, then you should suspect that the nerve at the top of the shoulder is compressed or extended or softened; and suspect that the joint will never fit in its socket.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	1. The dislocation that is towards the foot, and the knees, or thighs, if it is made by force, and extension of hands, and it is managed another hour; and it is cured as soon as it is healthy.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	2. And if after the cure there comes pain in the member, and later movement, if it uses the patient's bath many times, as long as that pain is alleviated, and returns to its first nature.
de la dislocation dou coute	3. of the dislocation that costs

de la dislocation dou talon	of the dislocation of the big toe
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The big toe is never used, and it is never fully dislocated, and it is often twisted.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee: li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	And the sign is that if the ankle is dislocated, and it is before the part where it is dislocated: the relocation is lighter, and it should be extended lightly with the hands when it is only weak.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient; et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	And when it is completely dislocated, if it is before the part where it is dislocated: the relocation is lighter, and it should be extended lightly with the hands when it is only weak. Then, if it is completely dislocated, you must seat the ankle right, and hold it with your hand on the leg, tugging on the foot; then, take the patella to your right hand, and then to your left, and lift it up, and hold it well at the top; and do this twice, as we have said, by bending and lifting the patella twice; and if it returns, it is well; if not, if it does not return, continue the extension, because it will return; and if it still does not return, make the patient lie on his back on the ground, and hold the knee firmly on the ground between the thighs, and let the patella drape over; then, mark the position of the patella with your hand, and other members extend the patella to their hands or to the patient's leg at the top of the patella; then extend each member equally, and the knee will be held between the patella and the patella; then place the dislocation in your hands, and mark the healthy leg on the opposite side, and the dislocation will return instantly.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	When it reaches its point, if it is covered with plaster and allowed to dry, and forms again, and the patient places the leg on the thigh, and covers the nerves that are under the ankle joint, so that the ligaments do not become too tight; then it is left alone for II or III days, and if the ligaments loosen, it is allowed to move; then it is re-dressed at the end of the fourth or fifth day, and if the patient does not return before this, it is considered a success.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess forms and comes out, it is necessary that you open it, as we have said elsewhere, as soon as it is healthy.
des dois	Of two things, one is that the
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the two are dislocated, if they can be extended well with effort, it is a light thing.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the dislocations are not in any way difficult to reduce, then you should try to put the shoulder on the table or on .ie. table totally straight, and place your foot on what is opened by these joints, then press with your foot on this, as it reheals; and when it is equalized, if there is no opening, then place a table at the head of the shoulder, then form the heel, and let it stay for three days, then remove it; and let it rest, until it is healthy.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	Of wound and dislocation together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	When wound and dislocation occur together, and it is seen that the wound is being restored, often the patient dies: if you are not presumptuous in your cure, whether you are skilled in the art and have not used it long, or whether you are pitiful and merciful and slow, do not be presumptuous; and begin with soothing apoplexy chaut, and leave the patient in God's hand, if you see no hope of health; and when you see hope, then reset the limb to the shoulder, unless the apoplexy chaut moves; and when the limb is at the shoulder, if it is painful, soothe it with gentle applications and cure the wound, as needed, with desiccants; and if there is a fracture with the dislocation, and the bones are broken, if the bones, and do as we have said in simple diseases; and do not enter into a path of despair, according to what we have said, for this is according to your creator's will, and for the wisdom of your heart.
Amen	I understand your request and will
